#### 5

## Advent of the English East India Company

#### History Alive!

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//21a23e5f-a274-469f-b7ef-ef94308d1324/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_61_313_802_844.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A40Z%2F-1%2F%2F315b22280a23b6f6b38410566fe61c7ec8d5ca17d5ab875cbd8e89288b6314b8" alt="Image" width="62%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//21a23e5f-a274-469f-b7ef-ef94308d1324/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_825_229_959_304.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A41Z%2F-1%2F%2F32b7fafa5e40ca904684c4053f5455955ca93360a9935466e7af652826c400dd" alt="Image" width="11%" /></div>

The Seven Years' War took place between 1756 and 1763. In this war, France and England fought against each other. Apart from them, Austria, Spain, Russia, Prussia and Portugal were the other nations that took part in this war. The war came to an end with the signing of the Treaty of Paris in 1763.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//21a23e5f-a274-469f-b7ef-ef94308d1324/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_1069_262_1129_323.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A41Z%2F-1%2F%2F220f13cc83abadc9dbc16afb666e44be31aa016305dfc165228c2e45dde1c81f" alt="Image" width="5%" /></div>

### Learning Outcomes

At the end of this lesson, learners will be able to:

trace the advent of English East India Company in India.

highlight the competition between the English and French East India Companies in India.

discuss the Carnatic Wars and the role they played in establishing British supremacy in India.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_491_172_781_414.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb3a73ddd82c4287da95b18a38a96aac1ea35b06bc3b91ee30009112ecaa435c5" alt="Image" width="24%" /></div>

War of Austrian Succession

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_870_173_1148_413.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F135324bd1e88b56b15c5d2e2eea898544b8d7c11827e4bde704b439ea8669c66" alt="Image" width="23%" /></div>

Seven Years' War

The British gradually gained political control over India through a number of battles against the rulers of Bengal, Awadh, Mysore and so on to. From traders, they became ‘rulers’.

The French were the biggest rival of the British in India, and there were frequent clashes between these two powers. Three Carnatic Wars were fought between 1746 and 1763 between the French and the British. These wars enabled the English East India Company (EEIC) to strengthen its control over southern India by defeating the French and successfully capturing the latter's strongholds in India. The Carnatic coast is the region in south India that lies between the Eastern Ghats and the Coromandel Coast. It is situated in the modern Indian states of Tamil Nadu, southeastern Karnataka and southern Andhra Pradesh.

### THE ENGLISH EAST INDIA COMPANY

The EEIC was a private concern, set up by British merchants. In 1600, it acquired the exclusive right to trade in the East from Queen Elizabeth I. Trade was profitable, and the Queen received a major share of these profits. In 1615, Thomas Roe visited the court of the Mughal Emperor Jahangir, who granted the Company many concessions. By 1623, factories were set up in Surat, Ahmedabad, Agra, Broach and Masulipatnam.

In 1639, Madras (now Chennai) was given to the British by a local ruler. The British established a post there. They fortified this post, which was named Fort St George. A few years later, King Charles II of England received the island of Bombay (now Mumbai), as a wedding gift, after marrying the Portuguese princess Catherine of Braganza. He gave the island of Bombay to the East India Company in 1688. Bombay became an important trading base for the East India Company by the middle of the 18th century.

At the end of the 17th century, the British had established a fortified factory in Calcutta (now Kolkata), called Fort William. Three presidencies were established in Madras Bombay and Calcutta, and a Governor was appointed for each of these.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_47_55_563_384.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F9f6de35ecffa97a0238a4cd93c74a1469006f08f008649ba87e737da500afbb8" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>

Fort William, Calcutta

### THE FRENCH EAST INDIA COMPANY

The French East India Company was formed in 1664. It established its headquarters in Pondicherry (now Puducherry). While the British were setting up factories along coastal India, the French East India Company founded other settlements in Mahe and Chandernagore.

### ANGLO-FRENCH RIVALRY: THE CARNATIC WARS

As the Dutch and Portuguese trading companies gradually lost their trading posts in India by the 18th century, Britain and France emerged as the two significant European powers in India. This was followed by contests for monopoly in trade rights and colonial possessions between the British and the French. The competition led to a series of wars, known as the Carnatic Wars in history. These wars also witnessed the participation of numerous independent Indian rulers who sought the support of Britain or France to aid their personal wars of succession.

##### First Carnatic War (1746-48)

The First Carnatic War took place between 1746 and 1748.

The British and the French were not only commercial rivals in India, but they were also political rivals in Europe.

The First Carnatic War in India started as a result of a war that broke out in Europe—the War of Austrian Succession in 1740—where Britain and France were on opposite sides.

##### Connecting Past with Present

Then Fort St George was the first English fortress in India. Founded in 1644 in the coastal city of Madras, it was built to aid British trading activity in south India. It gave birth to a new settlement called George Town, which included nearby villages and formed the city of Madras.

Now Fort St George serves as one of the administrative headquarters for the Legislative Assembly of Tamil Nadu. It also houses a garrison of the Indian army's troops

Joseph Dupleix, the French Governor, wanted to establish French supremacy over India.

Following hostilities between the British and the French, Dupleix captured Madras—a British stronghold.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_423_64_652_317.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa2f78aa49a094ee96396b4ea5458a3bd80436c805598dc04a9aee588f83b7c29" alt="Image" width="19%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">► Joseph Dupleix, the French Governor in India</div> </div>

When Dupleix refused to handover Fort St George to Anwaruddin Khan, the Nawab of Carnatic, the latter sent his troops. However, his army was defeated by the French.

The war in Europe came to an end in 1748, and a treaty was signed between Britain and France.

According to the terms of the treaty, Madras was returned to the British.

## Results

There were no territorial gains for either the British or the French, and the former territories were restored to these two parties.

The war enhanced the prestige of the French.

This is a sketch of Dupleix meeting Muzaffar Jang, the grandson of Nizam-ul-Mulk Asaf Jah.

##### Analysing Primary Sources

- What differences do you notice between the soldiers belonging to the two parties?

What do you gather about the relationship between the French and Muzaffar Jang from this picture?

##### Second Carnatic War (1749-1754)

Even after the conclusion of the First Carnatic War, Dupleix had the ambition to gain control over more territories in India.

He involved the French army in the regional rivalries between independent kings in the Carnatic region. This led to the Second Carnatic War, which lasted from 1749 to 1754.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_936_264_1175_606.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb8c8c54b984818b750bc9befdb11ee5c1b06b01db4ef894fa65376d4372f9d8c" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">Robert Clive</div> </div>

In this war, Robert Clive, then a young clerk in the EEIC, finally defeated the French forces.

Muhammad Ali, Anwaruddin's son, was made the Nawab of Carnatic by the British.

## Results

British power and prestige over the Carnatic region was restored.

☑ Dupleix was recalled to France.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_seal_box_775_1106_873_1214.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F143414a3a11a2f81967c5a98f3856c2f8f026b6ae8e3b28e1894c442e971e097" alt="Image" width="8%" />  <div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_seal_box_775_1106_873_1214.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F143414a3a11a2f81967c5a98f3856c2f8f026b6ae8e3b28e1894c442e971e097" alt="Image" width="8%" />  21st CENTURY SKILLS  </div>   </div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_774_1109_1164_1217.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb3c80cda2bcf45ac4afe578fd63893585d978a2d2e67a1fa2691eb0c2146549b" alt="Image" width="32%" /></div>

- visual literacy: analysing pictures

- critical thinking: observation

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_595_1219_1161_1525.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F52954db8d309f3e7ed23c4b2ed1f7b56f94fb62dad52a543089d70ebf7c342cc" alt="Image" width="47%" /></div>

#### Third Carnatic War (1756-63)

The Third Carnatic War lasted from 1756 to 1763. It took place as a result of the Seven Years' War, which broke out in 1756 in Europe between England and France.

The Seven Years' War led to an outbreak of hostilities between Britain and France in the Carnatic, and the peace established after the Second Carnatic War was broken.

The Third Carnatic War coincided with the Battle of Plassey (1757) in Bengal.

The British control of Bengal gave them access to funds to fight the wars against the French.

The Third Carnatic War was concluded once the Seven Years' War in Europe came to an end in 1763.

## Results

The French were completely defeated at the Battle of Wandiwash (1760) by the British.

The British became the dominant European power in southern India.

##### Debate

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_147_1079_240_1183.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F094034275499462bf1775fa73a934146b3657de943d5a21ba131ecb03d17e0c1" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>

critical thinking: cause and effect communication

##### And Discussion

What factors contributed to the Anglo-French rivalry?

### REASONS FOR THE BRITISH SUCCESS IN INDIA

Naval supremacy: The British navy was far superior to its French counterpart.

The British succeeded in winning the wars against their rivals for the following reasons:

Steady supply of arms and resources:

A superior navy enabled the British to receive a steady supply of arms and resources from their naval base in Bombay.

Financial stability: The conquest of Bengal and access to the land revenue from this region added to the British wealth.

EEIC—a private concern: The EEIC was free from government interference. The French Company, on the other hand, was subjected to constant interference from the French government, so they could not take major political decisions without the government's consent.

The British learnt a number of lessons from the wars they fought in India:

Political discord and quarrels among Indian rulers could be used to gain political and military control over India.

Large old-fashioned Indian armies were no match for well-trained modern European armies.

Indian soldiers could be easily recruited into the British Indian army and trained at very little cost.

The British gradually created a large powerful army with Indian sepoys and British officers. Thus, they were able to conquer most of the Indian subcontinent and establish themselves as the paramount power in India.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e7057c5b-2c8b-46cf-bd04-b43d530e3f4a/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_76_120_1124_461.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A36Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa0cce55432ad7f1ec5c23b1a176d431530ffce1ce242fc01004fd6d6a9c46c02" alt="Image" width="88%" /></div>

#### KEY WORDS

Factory: a trading post where goods are manufactured

Sepoys: Indian soldiers recruited into the British army

War of Austrian Succession: a war involving most European powers; it was fought between 1740 and 1748 to decide the ruler of the Austrian realm after the death of King Charles VI

☐ Siraj-ud-Daulah

☐ Dupleix

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a1ce4420-18fd-4fa1-9307-bd8d114fa868/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_669_192_897_498.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe77df2e8e67b2802581715181006baad4e35d3d5417f87ef989910441c25d035" alt="Image" width="19%" /></div>

Robert Clive

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a1ce4420-18fd-4fa1-9307-bd8d114fa868/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_935_195_1138_513.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2Ffa613c20dc9528a030ab76b6a92d42305dea815fc35a3a81a297964b5c748d9a" alt="Image" width="17%" /></div>

☐ Mir Qasim

In the 18th century, Bengal was considered the richest of all the Indian provinces. This prosperous and fertile land attracted traders from many European countries. Trading companies from Holland, France and England sent representatives to establish their respective trading settlements in Bengal.

In 1717, the Mughal emperor Farrukhsiyar issued a royal order or farman that granted the English East India Company (EEIC) the right to conduct duty-free trade in Bengal. This meant that the British could import and export goods to and from Bengal without paying any taxes to the government. They also had the right to issue dastaks or passes for the free movement of their goods. These favourable developments made the British settlement the largest and most prosperous of the European settlements. Its officials also amassed great wealth.

During the time of the Nawab of Bengal, Alivardi Khan, the British had established and fortified their factories in Bengal.

Alivardi Khan was succeeded by his grandson, Siraj-ud-Daulah. As soon as Siraj-ud-Daulah came to power, he ordered the British to pay taxes. The British refused to obey the order. This annoyed the Nawab. The Nawab's conflict with the British led to the Battle of Plassey, which was a landmark event in the history of Bengal.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a1ce4420-18fd-4fa1-9307-bd8d114fa868/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_893_733_1145_1185.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F31e3617fad3ffe6de0680586e8a8bad6b453b00cb9cdb6f6e371294b752b1053" alt="Image" width="21%" /></div>

▶ Alivardi Khan

##### BATTLE OF PLASSEY (1757)

The Battle of Plassey marked the beginning of the end of the rule of Nawabs in Bengal.

##### Causes

The following are the causes for the outbreak of the Battle of Plassey:

#### Fortifications

The French had established their settlement in Chandernagore. Anticipating war with the French, the British began to fortify their settlement in Calcutta without the Nawab's permission. Siraj-ud-Daulah was enraged at this direct challenge to his power. The Nawab asked the British and the French to pull down their fortifications. While the French agreed, the British refused. This led to a direct conflict between the Nawab and the British.

#### Capture of Calcutta

In 1756, Nawab Siraj-ud-Daulah marched towards Calcutta with a large army and captured Fort William, which was a British stronghold. However, Robert Clive soon recaptured Calcutta. Consequently, the Treaty of Alinagar was signed between the British and Siraj-ud-Daulah. According to the terms of the treaty, the Nawab restored trading rights and the city of Calcutta to the British. Rights to fortify Calcutta were also given to the British. However, the British were not satisfied and they wanted to place a puppet ruler on the throne of Bengal to suit their expansionist designs. The British under Clive, with the support of the former subedar of Bengal, Mir Jafar, presented a set of unreasonable demands to the Nawab, which made the battle inevitable.

#### The Battle

The Battle of Plassey was fought in June 1757 at Plassey (near Murshidabad). The British forces advanced under the leadership of Robert Clive, while Siraj-ud-Daulah led an army of about 50,000 men.

A large part of the Nawab's army was under the command of Mir Jafar, which did not participate in the battle. The Nawab himself left the battlefield after the death of his army commander, Mir Madan. The disheartened army was easily defeated. Later, Siraj-ud-Daulah was captured and put to death, and Mir Jafar was declared the Nawab of Bengal. The English gained control over Bengal by installing Mir Jafar as the puppet ruler.

#### Did You Know?

Jagat Seth was a rich Marwari businessman from Murshidabad during the rule of Nawab Siraj-ud-Daulah. Described by the official historian of the EEIC, Roben Orme, as the greatest banker in the known world, Jagat Seth conspired with Mir Jafar and Robert Clive against Siraj-ud-Daulah.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a1ce4420-18fd-4fa1-9307-bd8d114fa868/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_536_1051_622_1172.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F50e5d3f7781210efdc05118d5bfc7f9363c3ca55cea5ff23d7a5063330f73da8" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a1ce4420-18fd-4fa1-9307-bd8d114fa868/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_620_784_1060_1169.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F0d1a8a56eb997d554daf5061855fba1f638295d54efe4e6ae93aacdfe759997c" alt="Image" width="36%" /></div>

Jagat Seth's house in Murshidabad

##### Results of the Battle

The British victory at the Battle of Plassey had far-reaching consequences.

The EEIC acquired the undisputed right to trade in Bengal, Bihar and Orissa.

The Company was given zamindari rights over 24 parganas.

Mir Jafar paid a huge sum of money to the Company in return.

##### Importance of the Battle

The Battle of Plassey is considered to be a turning point in the history of India due to the following reasons:

It paved the way for the establishment of the British rule in India.

The Nawab of Bengal became a puppet in the hands of the British. The British transformed themselves from a trading company into a political power.

The vast resources of Bengal passed on to British hands. These resources were used to finance the Third Carnatic War and other battles for expansion in India.

##### Aftermath of the Battle

■ Mir Jafar was a Nawab only in name. He had responsibilities, but no power.

After the Battle of Plassey, the EEIC relentlessly plundered the seemingly inexhaustible resources and wealth of Bengal.

The Company directors ordered Bengal to pay for the expenses of administering the Bombay and Madras Presidencies.

■ Mir Jafar realised that it was impossible to meet the growing demands of the EEIC. He sought help from the Dutch East India Company and asked them to intervene.

■ The Dutch sent a force, but the British forces defeated them at Chinsurah—the Dutch stronghold.

The British soon deposed Mir Jafar and appointed Mir Qasim (Mir Jafar's son-in-law) as the new Nawab.

##### Reforms by Mir Qasim

Mir Qasim was an ambitious ruler. On becoming the Nawab, he immediately granted the zamindari rights over Burdwan, Midnapore and Chittagong to the British. Mir Qasim also undertook certain reforms to reorganise Bengal's administration, which was in a chaotic state.

■ Mir Qasim shifted his capital from Murshidabad to Monghyr, far from the British control.

He hired French officials to train and discipline the Bengal army. The new army was modern and well-equipped.

■ To prevent the misuse of duty-free trading privileges by the British, Mir Qasim abolished all duties on internal trade for Indians as well. This affected the British monopoly in trade and enraged them.

A series of wars broke out between Nawab Mir Qasim and the British. The most important amongst these wars was the Battle of Buxar.

#### THE BATTLE OF BUXAR (1764)

Mir Qasim was determined to recover the throne of Bengal. He formed an alliance with Shuja-ud-Daulah, the Nawab of Awadh, and Shah Alam II, the Mughal emperor. The combined forces met the British at the famous

Battle of Buxar in

However,

combined

the forces of

Indian

three allies

the completely

were

defeated by the

British at the

battle.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//6cbf0221-5ee3-42c6-b0dc-33abbfd0cd68/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_258_53_543_437.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F0a95699bcfb0c8375c57444036082746fc7cb8d5eb5ef47d6c69ba45e999d689" alt="Image" width="23%" /></div>

The Battle of Buxar marked the beginning of the British colonial oppression in Bengal. The following are some of the other results of this battle:

After the battle, the British became the absolute masters of Bengal.

The British gained political control over Awadh.

The Treaty of Allahabad (1765) was signed between Shah Alam II and Robert Clive. According to the treaty, the British obtained diwani or the right to collect revenue from Bihar, Bengal and Orissa.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//6cbf0221-5ee3-42c6-b0dc-33abbfd0cd68/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_31_1039_527_1462.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2Fcc73411cbd939f0035e5586d8515a84eb4a3ad61e1dea1bee064558fe2be5658" alt="Image" width="41%" /></div>

### Debate And Discussion

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//6cbf0221-5ee3-42c6-b0dc-33abbfd0cd68/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_788_27_1121_136.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2Fbe39c14b52ca81e2422186b79ca7c60b289e0e7eeb7db02a69c98ef6841552da" alt="Image" width="27%" /></div>

Do you agree that the Battle of Buxar marked the beginning of the British colonial oppression in Bengal?

Awadh was made a buffer state between the British possessions in Bengal and the Marathas.

The British agreed to defend the Nawab of Awadh against his enemies. However, the Nawab would have to pay for the expenses of the British troops.

### DUAL GOVERNMENT IN BENGAL (1765-72)

After the victories at Plassey and Buxar, the British became the real rulers of Bengal. A new  $ \underline{\text{administrative system was established}} $ in 1765. It was known as the  $ \underline{\text{Dual Government}} $ in Bengal.

### Drawbacks of the Dual Government

According to this system, the English enjoyed all the privileges of being a ruler, but had no responsibility. They had complete military power and the right to collect the revenue in Bengal and use it as they wished.

The Nawab, on the other hand, had to look after the administration, and law and order.

According to the system of Dual Government, the Nawab of Bengal also had to disband most of his army,

A small amount of revenue was given to the Nawab to run the civil administration.

☐ Actual administrative powers, and most importantly, the collection of revenue was controlled by the British.

##### Effects of the Dual Government

Such a system adversely affected the life of people in Bengal in the following ways:

Corruption of the officials who collected taxes grew.

Misery of the people, particularly peasants, increased.

The British were only interested in amassing wealth and did not bother about the welfare of the people. This was evident when the Great Famine of 1770 broke out in Bengal, in which more than one-third of the population perished.

#### End of the Dual Government (1772)

The defects of the Dual Government soon became visible to the British Parliament.

The system of administration and the economy of Bengal collapsed.

☐ The Company now directly took over the control of Bengal's administration.

☐ The Company appointed Warren Hastings as the new governor of Bengal.

By the Regulating Act of 1773, Warren Hastings became the first Governor-General of India.

Warren Hastings introduced various reforms and extended British territory far beyond Bengal.

Hastings is credited with laying the foundations of the British colonial rule in Bengal and introducing an organised system of government in Bengal.

<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">After Reading</div> </div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//6cbf0221-5ee3-42c6-b0dc-33abbfd0cd68/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_90_883_1185_1273.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F9edecdc77cc43503c8a8b9bafaf07e34fec733a62792d709381cd57e212d7719" alt="Image" width="92%" /></div>

#### KEYWORDS

Buffer state: a small state between two powerful states to keep them from fighting with each other

Diwani: the right to collect revenue from a certain area

Dual Government: a form of government introduced by Robert Clive in Bengal (1765), as a result of which there were two parallel governments in Bengal—the Nawab's and EEIC's

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//6cbf0221-5ee3-42c6-b0dc-33abbfd0cd68/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_0_1514_110_1613.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F7a120b63a0f4e02721b7c28ddb1d99da8df77e118da571d7279d44e5bf2c18b8" alt="Image" width="9%" /></div>

Farman: the order or decree by the government granted to the EEIC, which gave them the right to carry on duty-free trade in Bengal

Inexhaustible: never completely used up and therefore always available

Siraj-ud-Daulah: the Nawab of Bengal from 1756 to 1757 who was defeated by the British at the Battle of Plassey

Zamindari rights: the right to collect taxes in an assigned area

##### Synopsis of the Work of a Popular Historian

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//6cbf0221-5ee3-42c6-b0dc-33abbfd0cd68/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_790_1166_887_1273.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F090e69cdaf9afcb69c50836b46ace55407c3eee26937030ad3a75d2562a61db6" alt="Image" width="8%" /></div>

media literacy: academic skills

critical thinking: analysis

William Dalrymple is a popular historian; his work strives to make history interesting for the common people. Read his book, The Anarchy: The Relentless Rise of the East India Company. Write a synopsis of at least one chapter in your own words. A synopsis is a summary of a work that covers all the major points. Following are some pointers for writing a good synopsis:

Read the whole text and jot down your first summary in 50 words on the basis of your memory. Read the introduction to know the key points in each chapter. The first line of each paragraph will also point towards the key point in it.

- Highlight one sentence in each paragraph that you think is essential detail to understanding that section.

Write only key words as a summary of each point rather than whole sentences.

Use these key words to make your own short sentences to capture the points.

Try to keep the word count low.

How long is your synopsis?

## A British Building in Your Town/City

- initiative and self-direction: field trip

- communication

The British colonial presence was felt all across India. Even today, there are buildings, bridges and other structures built during the British times in all major towns and cities. Many of the buildings used as government offices were built by the British.

With the help of your school administration, arrange a tour of one such building/structure.

Find out as much of its history that you can.

Take pictures of the architectural features that interest you.

## Expansion of British Power in India

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b7b6403f-1511-48df-9e10-6109123a4820/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_170_304_819_772.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F9b336db6c26f2c4c1f008eadda352ae476adcbd1ebb3295a2855ed20fd0f758c" alt="Image" width="54%" /></div>

#### History Alive!

In the third Anglo-Mysore War, Tipu Sultan was defeated. According to the Treaty of Seringapatam (1792), he had to give away a large part of his kingdom to the British. He also had to pay a huge fine and send two of his sons as hostages to the British. Can you spot his sons in this picture?

#### Before Reading

#### Punjab (P) Maratha Territory (Ma)

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b7b6403f-1511-48df-9e10-6109123a4820/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_68_248_312_588.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F2c3d95542be85665f8aac7298741cae79c415fc5bd5822970506c642a5f89926" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>

☐ Ranjit Singh

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b7b6403f-1511-48df-9e10-6109123a4820/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_444_265_685_597.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe20fbeb254b8cfd01a837247ac4e8c35f16c6206e9f72cf1dbc8d1355d1f36e4" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>

Tipu Sultan

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b7b6403f-1511-48df-9e10-6109123a4820/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_810_281_1063_607.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F267ccd9371fa72351730c9eb683b24cdedae928464048ac03ec33d6451cb49f0" alt="Image" width="21%" /></div>

Narayan Rao

The three Carnatic Wars, the Battle of Plassey and the Battle of Buxar led to the establishment of the British as a major power in India. The Marathas, the State of Mysore and the Nizams of Hyderabad were three powers that fought amongst themselves for supremacy in the Deccan. The British joined this fight for supremacy, but with the aim of becoming the dominant power in India. This resulted in a number of wars between the British and the Indian rulers of south India, which are discussed in this chapter.

##### ANGLO-MYSORE WARS

The ruler of Mysore, Hyder Ali, was an efficient administrator, diplomat and an intelligent general. He introduced many reforms, which strengthened his kingdom. The rise of Mysore was a threat to the EEIC's policy of territorial expansion. As the Nizam of Hyderabad and the Marathas became rivals of Hyder Ali, the British took advantage of these rivalries to annex Mysore. Four wars were fought to subjugate Mysore.

##### First Anglo-Mysore War (1767–69)

In this war, the British formed an alliance with the Nizam of Hyderabad and the Marathas against Hyder Ali of Mysore. However, Hyder Ali was a great diplomat, who won over the Nizam and Marathas to his side. The British then faced a crushing defeat in the war that followed.

### Second Anglo-Mysore War (1780–84)

The British occupied the French port of Mahe, which was under Hyder Ali's jurisdiction, and prevented the merchants of Mysore from trading with Europe. This infuriated Hyder Ali, who declared war against the

British. Initially, the Marathas and the Nizam of Hyderabad were allies of Mysore, and together they captured Arcot. However, the British signed the Treaty of Salbai with the Marathas in 1782, whereby the latter withdrew their support to Hyder Ali.

Although Hyder Ali was defeated at Porto Novo (now Parangipettai in Tamil Nadu), the war did not end, as it was carried on by Hyder Ali's son, Tipu Sultan. The war ended with the signing of the Treaty of Mangalore in 1784.

##### Third Anglo-Mysore War (1790–92)

The Treaty of Mangalore did not resolve the conflict between the British and Tipu Sultan. In 1789, Travancore was attacked by Tipu Sultan. Travancore was an ally of the British and an important supplier of pepper.

The British again formed an alliance with the Marathas and the Nizam of Hyderabad. The Third Anglo-Mysore War broke out in 1790 and continued for two years. Eventually, Tipu was defeated and the Treaty of Seringapatam was signed in 1792.

### Fourth Anglo-Mysore War (1798–99)

In order to avenge his defeat in the Third Anglo-Mysore War, Tipu Sultan built up a large army against the British. Lord Wellesley, the Governor-General, introduced the policy of Subsidiary Alliance (discussed later in this chapter) to expand the British territory in India. Tipu refused to join this alliance. As a result, the Fourth Anglo-Mysore War broke out between Tipu and Wellesley in 1798.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b7b6403f-1511-48df-9e10-6109123a4820/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_111_770_1159_1500.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F84c1a64bc86d9ef20d64d41cf97272af17bcbae9b3cb74548cc120d39031981b" alt="Image" width="88%" /></div>

Clash between the British soldiers and the Mysore army during the Second Anglo-Mysore War

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b7b6403f-1511-48df-9e10-6109123a4820/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_32_62_549_732.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F277ab7c756791e99522986331444b34f0f77d77acaaf85fc3797afe2c9290519" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b7b6403f-1511-48df-9e10-6109123a4820/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_573_85_1104_738.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F24e1644890e05887604b9383b3922b7089e118348d80d84d526eecd05bee47a2" alt="Image" width="44%" /></div>

Geo-Skills: Locating Places cross-curricular connect: Geography 21st CENTURY SKILLS information literacy: map skills Compare the two maps given above and answer the following:

Did the territorial extent of the Mysore state decrease between the First and the Fourth Anglo-Mysore Wars?

Did the Peshwas have control over territories south of Goa during the First Anglo-Mysore War?

## Results

Tipu died defending his capital Seringapatam.

Half of the kingdom of Mysore was divided between the British and the Nizam of Hyderabad.

The other half was given to the earlier Raja of Mysore from whom Hyder Ali had seized power.

Thus, it took the British more than 30 years to completely subjugate Mysore. The British rule over the Deccan proved to be beneficial for them financially, economically and politically. The British territory now stretched from the Malabar to the Coromandel Coast.

##### ANGLO-MARATHA WARS

In 1773, the Maratha Peshwa Narayan Rao was murdered. A war of succession broke out between the supporters of the infant son of the deceased Peshwa, Madhav Rao II, and Raghunath Rao.

##### First Anglo-Maratha War (1775–82)

Raghunath Rao, also known as Raghoba, appealed to the British for help. The British readily agreed on the condition that they would receive the two important states of Salsette and Bassein, which were important ports. When Raghoba agreed, the British sent their troops to support him. The infant Madhav Rao II was under the able governorship of Nana Phadnavis, who was the leader of the Marathas. Under his leadership, the Maratha army defeated the British. The British forces were sent from Bengal and the war dragged on. No decisive result could be reached, and the Treaty of Salbai was signed in 1782.

There was peace between the British and the Marathas for 20 years. During this period, the British strengthened their position in Bengal and Mysore.

### Second Anglo-Maratha War (1803–05)

After the death of Peshwa Madhav Rao II in 1796, Baji Rao II became the new Peshwa. He was a weak and an inefficient ruler. To make matters worse for the Marathas, Nana Phadnavis died. This immediately led to an internal strife between the different Maratha families and chiefs. All of them fought to establish their influence at Poona (now Pune).

The disunity among the Marathas was immensely favourable for the British to gain control over the Maratha territory. In 1802, the Maratha faction led by the Holkars defeated the combined forces of the new Eshwa Baji Rao II, who was supported by the Scindias. This led the Peshwa to sign the Subsidiary Alliance with Lord Wellesley to seek British protection in order to retain control of his throne.

Lord Wellesley believed he could impose the policy of Subsidiary Alliance on all the other Maratha chiefs as well, since it had been signed by their nominal head. But he was mistaken. In 1803, the Scindias and the Bhonsles declared war against the British. The British, however, successfully defeated the combined forces of the Bhonsles and Scindias, and the latter were forced to accept the Subsidiary Alliance.

##### Third Anglo-Maratha War (1817-18)

In spite of signing the Subsidiary Alliance, Peshwa Baji Rao II wanted to free himself from British control. Thus, the Third Anglo-Maratha War started in 1817 when the Peshwa, with the support of the Holkars and Bhonsles, attacked the British Residency at Kirkee (now Khadki in Maharashtra). However, the Maratha forces were completely defeated by the British.

Debate And Discussion

What were the main reasons for the victory of the EEIC in the Anglo-Mysore and Anglo-Maratha Wars?

## Results

Baji Rao II was overthrown and exiled to Bithur near Kanpur and was given a pension.

The Marathas as a force were eliminated and were no longer seen as a threat to the British.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2353ee65-c124-42a1-a4f9-55431e5b4a85/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_37_70_613_437.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb7fac880a4e18ef1594db6620deece788e1e8c5f02d8de7c808fe37548994a1d" alt="Image" width="48%" /></div>

Indian camp scene during the Third Anglo-Maratha War

The reign of the Peshwas came to an end.

All Maratha territories were annexed to the British Empire.

The Bhonsles and Holkars signed the Subsidiary Alliance and ceded large parts of their territories to the British.

Satara, a small state, was carved out of the Maratha Empire, and a descendant of Shivaji was placed on the throne.

##### ANGLO-SIKH RELATIONS

The British knew that control over Punjab was essential for the establishment of the British Empire in the subcontinent. The growth of the Sikh power under Maharaja Ranjit Singh had made the EEIC anxious. So, they concluded a treaty with Ranjit Singh in 1809, known as the Treaty of Amritsar. Under the agreement, river Sutlej was recognised as the boundary between the Sikh and British territories.

After the death of Ranjit Singh, the political system organised by him broke down. The Sikh army assumed charge of the administration. The British felt that this period was suitable to annex Punjab. Two wars were fought, resulting in the annexation of Punjab by the British.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2353ee65-c124-42a1-a4f9-55431e5b4a85/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_665_87_1092_517.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F4777c6e3dd71f8f6d946ea34450d7be7cddca402a7a3bca6588ef0b0d4382511" alt="Image" width="35%" /></div>

► Raja Lal Singh led the Sikh forces during the First Anglo-Sikh War

##### The First Anglo-Sikh War (1845–46)

This war was fought after the Sikh army violated the Treaty of Amritsar. When the Sikhs crossed the Sutlej, the British Governor-General, Lord Hardinge, attacked the Sikh army. The Sikhs were completely defeated; their valiant and heroic efforts failed due to the treachery of their own men. After their defeat, the Sikhs were forced to sign the Treaty of Lahore (1846). This ended the First Anglo-Sikh War.

##### Second Anglo-Sikh War (1848–49)

After the First Anglo-Sikh War, the British had full control over Punjab. This aroused considerable resentment among the Sikhs, which resulted in the outbreak of a number of revolts.

The British Governor-General during this time was Lord Dalhousie. He soon declared war on the Sikhs and crushed the army, which was already reduced by the Treaty of Lahore. He annexed Punjab to the British Empire in 1849.

## Results

Punjab became a part of the British territory in 1849.

Maharaja Dalip Singh, the son of Ranjit Singh, was given a pension and sent to England.

The command of the Sikh army was taken over by the British officers.

### EXPANSION STRATEGIES

With the annexation of Punjab, the British conquest of India was complete. Most parts of India were either directly under the British or indirectly controlled by them through expansionist policies, such as the Subsidiary Alliance. Lord Wellesley and Lord Dalhousie were the Governor-Generals who adopted various strategies to increase British territories in India. Let us read to find out about these policies.

#### Lord Wellesley

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2353ee65-c124-42a1-a4f9-55431e5b4a85/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_504_24_1190_1015.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F3c3c4becc84c29112478a0087c68bfdb26a3344019a7238323716075f96ef811" alt="Image" width="57%" /></div>

Lord Wellesley initiated the system called the Subsidiary Alliance to expand the British dominion in India. The Subsidiary Alliance stated that if any Indian ruler felt insecure or threatened, he could appeal to the British for help and enter into an alliance with them. The British, in turn, promised to protect the ruler from external attacks and internal bolts. However, the Indian ruler had to ept certain terms and conditions that

- Was Malwa a part of the British territory in 1856?

- Which regions along the eastern coast of India were part of the British territory in 1856?

were put forward by the British. The first to enter into this alliance was the Nizam of Hyderabad. The Indian rulers lost their independence and were now controlled by the British

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2353ee65-c124-42a1-a4f9-55431e5b4a85/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_957_1168_1190_1462.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F48aa0599b7efd2f1742eca4362b400bd4791c2bb699b8782ca81da247236ed53" alt="Image" width="19%" /></div>

The clauses of the Subsidiary Alliance system were as follows:

British troops would be stationed permanently in the Indian ruler's territory.

It was compulsory for the ruler to house a British Resident in his court.

The ruler would have to pay for the maintenance of these troops. The payment could be made in cash or kind, or by ceding a part of the territory.

#### Did You Know?

The states that signed the Subsidiary Alliance were Hyderabad, Awadh, Tanjore, Mysore, Bhonsle, Peshwa, Sindhia, and many others.

The ruler could not employ any non-British Europeans in his service or dismiss those who were there.

The ruler could not enter into an alliance with any power without the consent of the British.

The ruler had to acknowledge the dominion of the British.

The policy of Subsidiary Alliance was advantageous for the British, but it adversely affected the Indians. These are outlined in the following table.

<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Advantages for the British</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Disadvantages for Indian Rulers</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>The British gained dominion over important territories as subsidiary payment.</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Indian rulers lost their independence and were completely controlled by the British.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>The Indian rulers maintained large armies for the British.</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Indian states became poor as the payment of subsidies drained their resources. When the administration collapsed, the British annexed the states.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Other European powers had little access to the courts of Indian rulers and could not influence them.</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>With British patronage and protection, the Indian rulers lost interest in the welfare of their own people, who suffered great misery and oppression.</td></tr></table>

##### Lord Dalhousie

Lord Dalhousie, who was the Governor-General of India during 1848–56, undertook a two-pronged approach to help the British expansion in India. The measures were as follows:

■ Doctrine of Lapse

Annexation on grounds of maladministration

##### Doctrine of Lapse

According to this doctrine, if a ruler died without a natural male heir, then the kingdom would pass or 'lapse' to the British. The rights of adoption were denied to the dependent states. Lord Dalhousie applied the Doctrine of Lapse to a number of states, such as Jhansi, Nagpur and Satara. The rulers of these states were given pensions, while their territories were annexed to the British Empire. As a result of this policy, the rulers of these states were extremely dissatisfied with the British.

### Annexation of Awadh on Grounds of Maladministration

Lord Dalhousie undertook indiscriminate annexation of regional kingdoms on grounds of maladministration. Awadh, one of the states to join the Subsidiary Alliance system, closely followed its terms and conditions. However, Dalhousie perceived the Nawab of Awadh, Wajid Ali Shah, to be an incompetent ruler.

Lord Dalhousie, therefore, annexed Awadh on grounds of inept governance in 1856. Yet, the administrative failure of Awadh was largely due to the operation of the Subsidiary Alliance system. During 1856-57, a large part of India came under British control. The British had effectively eliminated their Indian and European rivals and established themselves as the paramount power in India. The success of the British can be

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2353ee65-c124-42a1-a4f9-55431e5b4a85/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_871_50_1112_454.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A36Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe5516a52967a68723ee396d402ef9cefd6d29f1a4024ba2b8e1fe583f1c44564" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>

Wajid Ali Shah

ascribed to the lack of unity among Indian states. The greater military and financial resources of the EEIC also helped in the colonial expansion of the British.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2353ee65-c124-42a1-a4f9-55431e5b4a85/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_86_705_1122_1112.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A36Z%2F-1%2F%2F7aa4a7ccdf80ee0c74770cb9298bd71f37df1a86856578b5f527ab276a740e4b" alt="Image" width="87%" /></div>

#### KEYWORDS

Lord Hardinge: a British field marshal who defeated the Sikh army in the First Anglo-Sikh War; also the Governor-General of India from 1844 to 1848

Maladministration: inefficient or mismanaged administration

Treaty of Lahore: a peace treaty signed in 1846 between the British and the Sikh Maharaja Dalip Singh, marking the end of the First Anglo-Sikh War

Treaty of Mangalore: a peace treaty signed in 1784 between the British and Tipu Sultan, marking the end of the Second Anglo-Mysore War

Treaty of Salbai: a peace treaty signed in 1782 between the British and the representatives of the Maratha Empire, to settle the outcome of the First Anglo-Maratha War

Treaty of Seringapatam: a peace treaty signed in 1792 between the British and Tipu Sultan, marking the end of the Third Anglo-Mysore War

## Impact of the British Rule on India

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//40c9df84-b204-4bba-a3ef-9c60c8a81c28/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_118_319_823_764.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd062e68ec4804d2efd1037894fedc50c50c464588dc46a9c9f8e58113fd7f88e" alt="Image" width="59%" /></div>

□ IIT, Kharagpur

### ECONOMIC IMPACT OF THE BRITISH RULE

Towards the end of the 18th century, the EEIC was no longer a mere trading company. It had been transformed into a formidable colonial power controlling most of India. In order to retain control over their colony, the British established a system of administration for the maintenance of law and order, as well as for internal security.

Indian agriculture received special attention from the EEIC. This was primarily because the main source of the state income was land revenue. Moreover, it was the aim of the British government to establish India as an agricultural supplier of cheap raw materials to industries in England. The Company tried various experiments to maximise the land revenue, regardless of its oppressive impact on Indian peasants. Some of these land revenue policies were as follows:

■ Lord Cornwallis introduced the Permanent Settlement as a system of revenue collection in 1793 in Bengal, Bihar and Orissa.

The Ryotwari Settlement was introduced in Bombay and Madras Presidencies.

The Mahalwari Settlement was introduced in the northern part of the country, mainly in Uttar Pradesh and Punjab, where it had devastating effects.

### Features of Land Revenue Settlements

The land revenue settlements, regardless of the region of implementation, had certain common features. These were as follows:

Creation of a new social class of landlords who were loyal to the British

The Company was assured a fixed revenue or income without the trouble of collecting it from the peasants.

## NATIONAL COST-ORIENTAL HEARTE

The early 10th century, the British Government passed the Charter Act of 1812, industry the Company was required to spend the last rupees annually on the education of Indians. The Charter Act of 1813 sparked off a debate on education across England as people argued about what policy should he implemented to educate the people of India. One group argued that the traditional learning should be imparted in classical and regional Indian languages. These were the Orientalists. On the other hand, the Anglicists, led by Thomas Macaulay, insisted that the medium of instruction should be English and the education imparted should be Western.

## EDUCATIONAL REFORMS IN INDIA

Lord William Beetwick finally put an end to the debate on education by passing a conclusion that defined the education policy implemented by the British in India.

The new zamindari system encouraged absentee landlordism. This created a host of intermediaries between the state and the cultivator.

A class of corrupt moneylenders emerged as the intermediary class.

##### Impact of these settlements

The revenue settlements were exploitative and oppressive. The following points describe the negative effects of these revenue policies on agriculture in India:

Land became a saleable commodity, which could be bought, sold or mortgaged.

The zamindar, in order to collect more money, pressurised the peasants to pay more tax. Thus, he could set aside the extra revenue for himself.

Peasants were forced to pay revenue in times of famine as well. If they failed to pay the revenue on time, they were evicted from their land.

The zamindars as well as the British were completely indifferent to the suffering and exploitation of the peasants.

Frequent eviction from their land led to the growth of a class of landless peasants.

The peasants were forced to borrow money from the moneylenders in order to pay the revenue, even if their crops failed. Moneylenders added to the misery of the peasants. They lent money at high interest rates, which the poor peasants were unable to repay and fell into a cycle of debt.

Over cultivation of land depleted the fertility of the soil and resulted in the occurrence of regular famines.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e6c1f42b-767d-4b18-8479-404668f94212/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_seal_box_880_38_973_133.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F47b5c3db79419a8700c6f9d9ec6e75dce873d2fbdd269bc1795573440e9f4630" alt="Image" width="7%" />  <div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e6c1f42b-767d-4b18-8479-404668f94212/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_seal_box_880_38_973_133.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A32Z%2F-1%2F%2F47b5c3db79419a8700c6f9d9ec6e75dce873d2fbdd269bc1795573440e9f4630" alt="Image" width="7%" />  21st CENTURY SKILLS  </div>   </div>

##### Debate

##### And Discussion

How did the different types of revenue settlements for different areas affect the life of the people of India?

#### Impact on Industries

Indian industries also suffered a great setback under the British colonial rule. The British government, in the early years of the 18th century, imposed heavy duties on Indian textile imports to Britain. On the other hand, British machine-made goods entered India duty-free or at a nominal cost. The introduction of such a policy of one-way free trade made Indian goods very costly. It resulted in a significant decrease in sale for the Indian artisans and loss of their livelihoods.

##### Transport and Communication

The British realised that to consolidate their position in India, the development of proper communication facilities was necessary. They built an elaborate network of roads, canals and railway lines to connect all major cities, ports and agricultural centres. Metalled roads were built, and the railway system was introduced.

##### Benefits of Improved Transport System

The improved transport system ensured more efficient governance for the British. They could quickly transport troops and rapidly communicate to quell revolts and other disturbances.

It became easier to transfer raw materials and finished goods for the promotion of trade and commerce.

### Connecting Past with Present

Then In 1853, the first railway line from Bombay to Thane was inaugurated. In the same year, the post and telegraph department was set up. The first telegraph line was opened from Calcutta to Agra.

Diesel locomotives have replaced steam engines on trains in India.

The postal department in India has also grown in leaps and bounds since independence. Presently, there are more than 1.5 lakh post offices that are in operation all over India. The Government of India is actively involved in modernising the transport and communication system in India, while retaining its affordability.

Do you think the transport and communication system in India needs further modernisation? Give reasons for your answer. If yes, suggest certain ways of modernisation.

Although the transport and communication system was established to further British imperialist designs, it benefited Indian merchants as well. They now had an efficient system through which they could export raw materials such as cotton, jute and indigo and import finished goods from Europe. The merchants made a lot of profit and became very wealthy.

Another advantage of the transport and communication system was that it increased the communication between Indians living in different regions of the country. This in turn infused a sense of unity and resulted in the growth of nationalism—a development which in due course brought an end to the British rule in India.

#### Economic Exploitation of India

The British government drained the Indian economy and exploited it to the maximum. The exploitation took the following forms:

The British bought raw materials at cheap prices and sold their manufactured goods at high prices, flooding the Indian markets with their products. This led to the ruin of small-scale cottage industries.

The peasants were forced to pay high taxes, leading to increase in the poverty level and discontent. Therefore, a number of peasant revolts and uprisings took place.

The workers were paid low wages. The British made no effort to improve industry or agriculture in India.

India's wealth was being systematically drained away to England.

### ANGLICIST-ORIENTALIST DEBATE

In the early 19th century, the British government passed the Charter Act of 1813, whereby the Company was required to spend one lakh rupees annually on the education of Indians. The Charter Act of 1813 sparked off a debate on education across England as people argued about what policy should be implemented to educate the people of India. One group argued that the traditional learning should be imparted in classical and regional Indian languages. These were the Orientalists. On the other hand, the Anglicists, led by Thomas Macaulay, insisted that the medium of instruction should be English and the education imparted should be Western.

### EDUCATIONAL REFORMS IN INDIA

Lord William Bentinck finally put an end to the debate on education by passing a resolution that defined the education policy implemented by the British in India.

### Development of Western Education

#### Analysing Primary Sources

In 1835, Thomas Macaulay's Minute on Indian Education condemned the use of Indian languages. Moreover, the study of Indian forms of knowledge was also not encouraged.

Thomas Macaulay (Law Member of the Governor-General's Council) suggested the creation of a class of Indians who would act as a link between the ruler and the ruled.

This class was also expected to provide cheap human resources for lower levels of the administration.

Consequently, it was clear that the knowledge of English was necessary for Indians.

Macaulay insisted that Western education should be introduced and imparted across British territories in India through the medium of English.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e6c1f42b-767d-4b18-8479-404668f94212/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_961_721_1158_992.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F37766da572c71a5c480dfaed7761e223b20cd1cbed32357a5bcf5e8540990532" alt="Image" width="16%" /></div>

Thomas Macaulay

##### critical thinking: comprehension, analysis

We must at present do our best to form a class who may be interpreters between us and the millions whom we govern; a class of persons, Indian in blood and colour, but English in taste, in opinions, in morals, and in intellect. To that class we may leave it to refine the vernacular dialects of the country, to enrich those dialects with terms of science borrowed from Western nomenclature, and to render them by degrees, fit vehicles for conveying knowledge to the great mass of the population.

### Wood's Despatch on Education

Charles Wood, the President of the Board of Control, was a British government official responsible for overseeing the EEIC.

In 1854, he sent a despatch to the Governor-General of India, Lord Dalhousie.

Known as the Wood's Despatch, it laid the foundation on which the modern system of education in India developed.

It was declared that the aim of the British government was the promotion of Western education.

Wood prepared a comprehensive report with several recommendations in order to improve the system of education in India.

For higher education, the medium of instruction was to be English.

Almost all the proposals in the Wood's Despatch were diligently implemented.

English medium schools were set up.

Later, girls' schools were set up and brought under the control of the Government of India. Several grants

were also provided for the promotion of women's education.

Three universities for higher education were established in Calcutta, Bombay and Madras in 1857.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//e6c1f42b-767d-4b18-8479-404668f94212/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_275_1110_529_1472.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F433dd111dc7a8e0e23b890c4c4c614461166c92eac502bf71dead88d1fd90328" alt="Image" width="21%" /></div>

Charles Wood

### Impact of Western Education in India

The introduction of Western education in India had both negative and positive effects on the Indian people. Study the given table to know about these effects.

<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Negative Effects of Western Education</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Positive Effects of Western Education</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Led to complete Westernisation of the educational system</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Created awareness among Indians about being subjected to a foreign rule</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Caused replacement of the indigenous methods of education</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Resulted in the growth of the ideas on democracy, liberty and fraternity among educated Indians</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Led to the creation of English-educated Indians, who mostly became low-ranking clerks</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Created national consciousness and the desire for independence brought on by the knowledge of Western nationalist events, such as the French Revolution and the American War of Independence</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Resulted in the rejection of Indian culture and preference for all things British among the Westernised Indians</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>People of different regions and languages could communicate in English and share common problems and create awareness about the ill-effects of the British rule</td></tr></table>

#### KEYWORDS

Absentee landlordism: when a person owns a piece of property and rents it out for profit, but does not live within the local region of the property

Anglicists: those who felt that education imparted to the Indians should be Western, and the medium of instruction should be English

Formidable: inspiring fear or respect through use of power

Imperialist: extension of rule or authority over a foreign nation

Nationalist: relating to those who are inspired by ideas of liberty and equality to work for a united nation

Orientalists: those who argued in favour of traditional Indian education in classical Indian languages

• art-integrated learning

In the colonial period, the Dutch, French and British collected information about the flora and fauna of India, asking artists to make intricate sketches depicting them. Many Europeans serving in India and their wives sketched and painted as a hobby. The flora and fauna of India was thus well-documented in this period.

(from left to right: green-winged macaw; flying squirrel; comb drake; black stork, c. 1780)

#### Arrange a Bird Corner in your Balcony/Garden

#### Materials required:

In the present times, we can continue to appreciate and gain knowledge about the biodiverse flora and fauna of our country. These activities will help you to do that.

2 shallow, wide-mouthed clay pots from the local potter

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2e711e65-a95b-4bb5-a33b-b61413db8a62/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_947_1133_1102_1282.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A36Z%2F-1%2F%2F01429a4a13cc0122cbaa5736480a32716bcafe1230c9a42cb79447f0c3332cd4" alt="Image" width="13%" /></div>

Clean water

Bird seeds

## Method:

Arrange these in a relatively quiet section of your balcony or garden. Keep your movement around this area to the minimum. Fill one clay pot with fresh water and the other one with bird seeds.

##### Over a period of time:

Observe the types of birds that visit your bird corner.

• Photograph as many of these birds as possible.

You can sketch these birds like the British did too.

Learn the names of the birds that visit—both local and botanical names.

Study the habits of each type of bird. What sound does it make? Which time of the day does it come? Which month of the year does it come?

##### Leaf Safari Activities

The Europeans in colonial India even employed Indians to sketch and paint the flora and fauna to illustrate their own books. One such artist was Rungiah, who sketched Indian plants (see pictures given here).

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2e711e65-a95b-4bb5-a33b-b61413db8a62/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_252_566_607_1072.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A37Z%2F-1%2F%2F513edbf32e4eee856aec4a3d1bb07a5e04ba84013f129711d8d78fddc938df93" alt="Image" width="29%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//2e711e65-a95b-4bb5-a33b-b61413db8a62/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_698_575_1024_1072.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A37Z%2F-1%2F%2Fdfa731e1883873325ff31c161f2ebb12ff93889edf6bb98cb901c528dd698722" alt="Image" width="27%" /></div>

Leaves come in various shapes and sizes. The learners may study the different kinds of leaves through online and textual sources.

With a basic understanding of the different types of leaves, they may be allowed a 'leaf safari' in their school campus. They can pick up the different kinds of fallen leaves that they find and identify the names.

Put a leaf between two tracing papers, and place this within some newspapers. Keep them in the corner of the classroom to dry, weighed down by heavy books. Change the newspapers every 4-5 days, till the leaves are completely dry. Now, the dry leaves can be pasted on a chart paper. All the information that the learners know about each leaf can be written beneath it.

##### Worksheet 2

I. Give reasons for the following statements.

1. Though Bombay was controlled by the Portuguese, the EEIC acquired it.

### The Great Uprising of 1857

### History Alive!

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//4092302f-e4e3-4782-a263-5d04c347f8e0/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_28_230_787_720.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A49Z%2F-1%2F%2F8e59af1b059de95b40ff732a28fe88cb511155b8833f8a7876b168de98e18d4d" alt="Image" width="63%" /></div>

The Revolt of 1857 began in Meerut and spread to Delhi, Lucknow, Kanpur, Jhansi, Gwalior and Arrah. Though the British were able to suppress the revolt, it succeeded in sowing the seeds of Indian nationalism. Hence, it is also called the First War of Independence.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//4092302f-e4e3-4782-a263-5d04c347f8e0/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_811_221_944_283.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A49Z%2F-1%2F%2F7f18f01e270bff09800ff629ddc022ba59cc2df1eb5a274da81a1c509f41e266" alt="Image" width="11%" /></div>

Bahadur Shah Zafar

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ac5e2b3e-09d2-487b-acaf-a436ee25c10b/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_880_189_1127_525.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A31Z%2F-1%2F%2F6df8424eed27d91104489ebe127f7fba45689cc97e565b32ff06ea1319e66eda" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>

Lord Cornwallis

The Battle of Plassey marked the first step taken by the British to gain political control over India. During the next 100 years, the British used their financial and military strength to gain control over most of the Indian subcontinent.

The British methods were unfair, oppressive and exploitative, and there was enormous resentment against the British rulers among the Indians. This culminated in the Uprising of 1857, referred to by the British historians as the Sepoy Mutiny. For many Indians, it came to be known as the First War of Independence.

#### REVOLT OF 1857: CAUSES

Various causes—political, economic, socio-religious, military and immediate—were responsible for the uprising of 1857. These causes created much displeasure towards the British rule in India.

The unjust territorial annexations carried out by Lord Dalhousie through the policy of Doctrine of Lapse created anger and resentment towards the British.

#### Political Causes

Denial of the right to inherit Mughal property by Bahadur Shah's successors or to use imperial titles was a source of concern.

Annexation of Awadh, despite its adherence to the Subsidiary Alliance, increased the insecurity of Indian rulers.

Rulers mistrusted the British as they were quick to break treaties.

##### Economic Causes

Heavy taxes due to the land revenue systems, such as the Permanent and Ryotwari Settlements, increased the misery of peasants.

Peasants were forced to grow crops such as indigo, which suited the needs of the British economy.

British strategy of buying cheap raw materials from India and selling British manufactured goods at low rates damaged the Indian economy.

Livelihoods of artisans were adversely affected as they could not compete with duty-free British manufactured goods sold at cheaper rates.

Annexation of Indian states led to the confiscation of zamindari rights, and caused the zamindars to lead the rebels.

#### Socio-religious Causes

Indians disliked being treated as inferior people and excluded from high administrative posts by the British.

Many Indians were alarmed by the increasing activities of Christian missionaries in India.

Social reforms such as the abolition of sati and widow remarriage were seen as the British's interference with traditional Indian values and customs.

Sections in Indian society objected to the prominence given to Western education at the cost of traditional learning.

#### Military Causes

Harsh treatment of the sepoys by the British officers created discontent.

Many Indians, in those days, believed that they would lose their caste and religion if they crossed the sea. In 1856, the Company passed an act, known as the General Service Enlistment Act. According to this Act, every new recruit had to serve overseas, if ordered. It hurt the religious sentiments of the sepoys.

The Indian sepoys were paid much less than the British soldiers.

#### Immediate Cause

The situation worsened with the introduction of Enfield rifles in the army. The greased cartridges for these rifles had to be bitten off before being inserted into the rifle.

Rumours had spread in the sepoy camps that the grease contained fat from pigs and cows. Hindu and Muslim sepoys therefore objected to using them.

When the British severely punished and imprisoned sepoys for refusal to use the cartridges, the sepoys were enraged.

#### THE REVOLT

The sepoys at the Meerut cantonment were angered at the humiliating treatment of their fellow comrades. They rose in revolt, attacked the jail and freed the sepoys. Many of the sepoys marched to Delhi, where they were joined by the sepoys of the local army. The revolt spread throughout Delhi. The rebel forces proclaimed Bahadur Shah Zafar as the leader of the revolt and celebrated the revival of the Mughal Empire.

The British reinforcements soon arrived from Punjab, and Delhi was recaptured. Hundreds of Indians were killed, and many were hanged without trials. Bahadur Shah was taken prisoner, tried and exiled to Rangoon in Burma (now Myanmar).

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ac5e2b3e-09d2-487b-acaf-a436ee25c10b/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_81_32_831_938.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F5fd825f8ad2372e906271fee44b4610662cebf19f05433d224a4ee1f7e4a773f" alt="Image" width="63%" /></div>

The news of the events at Delhi spread rapidly, provoking uprisings among sepoys in many districts, including the North-Western

Bibighar in Kanpur—a site of the Revolt of 1857

Province, central India and Bihar. In many cases, it was the behaviour of the British military and civilian authorities that accelerated discontent among the Indians.

##### Awadh

After Delhi, a rebellion erupted in Awadh (modern-day Uttar Pradesh), which had been annexed by Lord Dalhousie. The rebel forces besieged the residence of the British Commissioner, Sir Henry Lawrence. With the arrival of British reinforcements, the rebels were defeated and Lucknow was recovered by the British.

##### Kanpur

In Kanpur, sepoys rebelled and besieged the British entrenchment. The leader of the Kanpur Revolt was Nana Sahib, the adopted son of Baji Rao II. His victory was short-lived as the British soon recaptured Kanpur and Nana Sahib escaped. His general, Tantia Tope, continued the struggle.

#### Did You Know?

In Arrah (Bihar), Kunwar Singh, a royal Kshatriya, played a leading part in the Revolt of 1857 at the age of 80 years.

Along with Tantia Tope, Lakshmibai then mounted a successful assault on the city-fortress of Gwalior. The treasury and the arsenal of the fort were seized. After taking Gwalior, Lakshmibai marched east to confront a British counterattack. She fought a fierce battle, but was killed in the combat.

### Debate And Discussion

Imagine that you were one of the leaders in the Revolt of 1857. Explain how you would have planned to keep the British away from your territory.

Such resolute defiance of the British made the Rani of Jhansi a symbol of bravery and courage and a source of inspiration for the future freedom fighters of India.

At the end of 1857, the British had begun to gain ground in the major centres of the revolt. In 1858, a peace treaty was signed and the revolt ended.

### CAUSES FOR FAILURE OF THE REVOLT

The following were major causes for the failure of the revolt:

The revolt lacked coordination, and the rebels had no common plan of action.

#### Analysing Primary Sources

The rebels lacked centralised leadership. There was no one to give proper direction to the revolt. The leaders were more interested in their personal territorial gains

These were not mutineers but residents of the city, who trusted to our well-known mild rule for pardon. I am glad to say they were disappointed.
