as they didn't yet have the idea of a nation state.

The rebel forces lacked suitable weapons. The outdated Indian arms were no match for the modern British weaponry. Moreover, the Indian rebels also lacked financial resources.

The revolt was localised. It did not spread to all parts of the country. Southern parts of India remained unaffected by the revolt. Many princes and zamindars remained loyal to the British. Peasants, who constituted a majority of the population, remained indifferent to the revolt.

#### EFFECTS OF THE REVOLT

The Revolt of 1857 had far-reaching effects in the history of India.

Queen Victoria issued her famous Proclamation in 1858. By this Proclamation, India passed directly under the control of the British Crown.

A new office of the Secretary of State was created.

The powers of the Governor-General were increased and the office of the Viceroy was created in its place. The first Viceroy of India was Lord Canning.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ac5e2b3e-09d2-487b-acaf-a436ee25c10b/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_341_1033_635_1403.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F4647d6cbf5da39507a3e8831da76e8d31a52af6c5fcbe0b0d393bc2d1422a92c" alt="Image" width="24%" /></div>

Lord Canning

The Queen's Proclamation abolished the Doctrine of Lapse. Rights of adoption were granted to the Indian rulers and annexed territories were returned to the princes.

The Proclamation stated that the treaties drawn with the Indian states would be honoured.

Queen Victoria promised to look after the welfare of the Indian people.

The British government promised not to interfere in the social and religious customs of the people.

The British Indian army was reorganised and strengthened, and the number of British soldiers in it was increased.

The Revolt of 1857, for the first time, created the feeling of nationalism among Indians. The sacrifice and heroism of its leaders inspired the people. Even though the revolt failed to achieve its main objective of driving out the British from India, it was successful in creating awareness about the exploitative nature of the British rule in India. Hence, the revolt is perceived by some historians

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//ac5e2b3e-09d2-487b-acaf-a436ee25c10b/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_946_903_1189_1361.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F9bc23cfee11baf4ebbc4cccd50de41529352493871ba56541408ad38b2a54d74" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>

Queen Victoria

as the first step in achieving independence for India.

## Comparative History

### The Opium Wars

The Opium Wars took place between China and the western countries over the issue of the Opium trade. The First Opium War was fought between China and Britain during the Opium trade. The Second Opium War was fought by Britain and France against China in the second Opium war was defeated in both of these wars.

### KEY WORDS

Besiege: to surround a castle or a city with an army in order to prevent the people inside from receiving food and water

strong walls, towers, etc., built around a place in order to defend it against attack

prising of 1857: a revolt in India in 1857, which was the culmination of decades of resentment against the exploitation, oppression and injustice of the British rule

## Reform Movements in India under the British Rule

##### History Alive!

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b13ff0bb-aced-45a1-894d-c783874a3bb6/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_35_243_223_512.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A36Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe6adff7892fa0f61381f95612d36e4aaefcb696efe09c020b3569351885dde38" alt="Image" width="15%" /></div>

Dayanand Saraswati

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b13ff0bb-aced-45a1-894d-c783874a3bb6/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_278_239_491_494.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A36Z%2F-1%2F%2Fc42763fe992bce7617a4841de96228b61431ade37ff5abb91367ffe97839e2b4" alt="Image" width="17%" /></div>

□ Annie Besant

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b13ff0bb-aced-45a1-894d-c783874a3bb6/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_543_261_746_514.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A36Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb853b7d013addb057720a26d96d18810c26d544dcaff5ab1ece3cfb2570620e2" alt="Image" width="17%" /></div>

Vivekananda

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b13ff0bb-aced-45a1-894d-c783874a3bb6/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_803_282_1013_520.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A36Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb728623c9151af12628d5038494fa35d2294123f661a0240df597217d90e3435" alt="Image" width="17%" /></div>

B.R. Ambedkar

With the establishment of British rule, the demand for using English as the language of administration and education also increased. Many individuals and organisations began to study both classical and vernacular languages. In 1817, Hindu College was founded in Calcutta (now Kolkata). In 1856, Elphinstone College was established in Bombay (now Mumbai). These institutes were primarily responsible for producing a large section of the English-educated elite Indians.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//b13ff0bb-aced-45a1-894d-c783874a3bb6/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_20_1044_475_1416.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A36Z%2F-1%2F%2Ffa0d37c8f7820dd0897baf6d1422d97cd21480d8c710dd2880d750482c0697cf" alt="Image" width="38%" /></div>

Elphinstone College, Bombay

Besides education, Western models of social etiquette, dress and eating habits also began to be followed by many Indians. This led to a conflict between the traditional sections of Indian society and the pro-Western Indians.

Many British administrators and thinkers were very critical of the traditional practices and attitudes towards women prevalent in Indian society. This critique led many Indians to take a closer look at their own society and to initiate a series of reform movements.

### SOCIO-RELIGIOUS REFORM MOVEMENTS

During the 19th century, many Indian reformers emerged and advocated deliberate changes in the traditional social, cultural and religious attitudes and customs to eliminate narrow-minded practices in Indian society. These Indian reformers were the leading participants in the social and cultural revival or renaissance, which took place in the 19th century. The renaissance began in Bengal

and quickly spread to different parts of the country. It was brought on by the following factors:

Realisation of unjust and unacceptable

social customs by some Indians

Spread of scientific and rational ideas

due to Western education

Sense of pride among Indians for their past achievements

Ability of the middle class to demand reforms

### REFORM MOVEMENTS IN BENGAL

Bengal was one of the first regions to witness a series of reform movements. Let us read about some of the important reformers of this region.

##### Brahmo Samaj

Raja Ram Mohan Roy was a well-read scholar. He believed that all religions preached similar fundamental truths. He condemned priests who exploited and misled people into practising unfair customs. He fought against many evil practices in Hindu society, such as polygamy, female infanticide, rigid caste system, sati and child marriage.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d2c4910f-5a20-4f60-bf37-cc335016735c/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_88_1138_602_1472.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A45Z%2F-1%2F%2F41f94f0b8a2c13c28a0765060597da4e2d3f233185563fe45be7434386d4310c" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>

▶ A painting from the 18th-century showing sati or widow-burning

Raja Ram Mohan Roy founded the Brahmo Samaj in 1828. The reforms advocated by the Brahmo Samaj under the leadership of Raja Ram Mohan Roy were as follows:

Abolition of sati and child marriage

Widow remarriage

Rejection of the caste system

Modern education for all

Equality of rights for women, and their right to property

The Brahmo Samaj was an early attempt to reform the Hindu society. It found many followers amongst educated young men who were influenced by the ideas of liberty and fraternity.

Raja Ram Mohan Roy believed that Western education could help in the spread of modern and progressive ideas. This could bring about social change. He helped to establish the Hindu College (known today as Presidency University) in Calcutta and the Vedanta College.

Raja Ram Mohan Roy worked tirelessly to reform society and regenerate feelings of nationalism among Indians. His efforts persuaded the then Governor-General, Lord William Bentinck, to pass a law banning sati, which made it a crime punishable by law.

##### Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar

Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar was a humanist who championed the cause of the poor and the underprivileged. He campaigned for the following reforms:

Deeply pained by the plight of widows in Bengal, he took up their cause. This earned him many enemies, but he

refused to give up. Finally, the Widow

Remarriage Act was passed in 1856.

He opposed the monopoly of the Brahmanas on the study of Sanskrit and admitted non-Brahmanas to its study.

He felt that emancipation of women was crucial for the reformation of the Indian society.

He helped Drinkwater Bethune establish one of the first schools for girls in Calcutta in 1849. He also introduced the study of Western philosophy in the Sanskrit College of Calcutta. He went on to open more schools for girls.

### Swami Vivekananda and Ramakrishna Mission

Swami Vivekananda was a disciple of Ramakrishna Paramahamsa. Ramakrishna's teachings were simple and attracted many followers. He preached that all religions

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d2c4910f-5a20-4f60-bf37-cc335016735c/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_9_861_158_1099.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A46Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb0e278d4dbe82ab5d89560c521a71f08c8a6d28224f55212f107674233aabe57" alt="Image" width="12%" /></div>

Ramakrishna Paramahamsa

have different paths to reach the one true God. He also said that service to mankind was service to God. One of his most famous disciples was Narendra Nath Datta, who later came to be known as Swami Vivekananda.

Some of the beliefs of

Swami Vivekananda were as follows:

Essential unity of all religions

Importance of religious tolerance, brotherhood, peace and harmony

Condemnation of the caste system, social and economic inequalities, ritualism and superstitions

Regeneration of Indians through self-discipline and self-realisation of one's responsibility to society

Upliftment of the position of women

Vivekananda established the Ramakrishna Mission and other educational institutions to help reform Indian society and spread education.

### REFORM MOVEMENTS IN WESTERN INDIA

Western India also witnessed a number of social reform movements. The Prarthana Samaj and the Arya Samaj are noteworthy among them. Let us read more about these movements and the reformers who initiated them.

##### Prarthana Samaj

The reform movements in western India were led by Mahadev Govind Ranade and R.G. Bhandarkar. In the 1860s, they were instrumental in establishing the Prarthana Samaj in Bombay.

The Prarthana Samaj campaigned for the following reforms:

Abolition of child marriage

☑ Spread of education

Support of widow remarriage

Education for women

Hindu-Muslim unity

##### Did You Know?

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d2c4910f-5a20-4f60-bf37-cc335016735c/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_733_1169_818_1263.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A47Z%2F-1%2F%2Ffe145d44159ec95d88a15242cf154e30171dc5d1969fd33efc066304ec58e84f" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>

Ramabai Ranade was one of the first women's rights activists in the 19th-century India. At the age of 11, her marriage with Mahadev Govind Ranade changed her life completely. Mahadev Ranade was himself a social reformer, and he encouraged Ramabai to educate herself after their marriage.

## Analysing Primary Sources

We aim to turn this MAO College into a University similar to that of Oxford or Cambridge. Like the churches of Oxford and Cambridge, there will be mosques attached to each College. It will be mandatory on boys in residence to join the congregational prayers (namaz) at all the five times. Students of other religions will be exempted from this religious observance. Bad and abusive words which boys generally pick up and get used to, will be strictly prohibited. Smoking of cigarette or huqa and the chewing of betel shall be strictly prohibited. No corporal punishment or any such punishment as is likely to injure a student's self-respect will be permissible.

### REFORM MOVEMENTS IN SOUTH INDIA

Kandukuri Veeresalingam was a prominent social reformer from South India. He fought for the education and upliftment of women and widow remarriage.

Sree Narayana Guru was another important spiritual and social reformer from south India. He denounced the rigid caste system prevailing in Indian society. He also stressed on the need for spiritual and social upliftment of the oppressed classes.

### SYED AHMAD KHAN AND THE ALIGARH MOVEMENT

Syed Ahmad Khan was a Muslim educator, jurist and author. He was a progressive realist and the principal motivating force behind the revival of the condition of the Indian Muslims in the late 19th century. He started the Aligarh Movement.

Syed Ahmad realised the need to promote Western education amongst Muslims. In order to achieve this, he founded the Muhammadan Anglo-Oriental College at Aligarh

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d2c4910f-5a20-4f60-bf37-cc335016735c/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_761_640_1009_905.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A49Z%2F-1%2F%2Ff5ce609557b32c00d2ee4251520bfc6f7c1474019021deace5be823d0abda338" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>

Syed Ahmad Khan

in 1877. This college became a centre for modern learning, and later grew into the Aligarh Muslim University.

Syed Ahmad organised the All-India Muhammadan Educational Conference, which met annually at different places to promote education and to provide Muslims with a common platform. He felt that the condition of the Muslims would improve if they had access to Western scientific learning.

##### REFORMS AMONG THE SIKHS

The Singh Sabha, a 19th-century Sikh movement, was set up in Amritsar and

Lahore to carry out socio-religious reforms among the Sikhs. The reforms undertaken by the Singh Sabha were as follows:

The Khalsa College was set up in Amritsar.

A number of schools were started to promote the Gurmukhi script and Punjabi literature.

The Akali Movement was later launched to purify Sikh practices and oust the British from India.

##### REFORM MOVEMENTS: IMPACT

As a group, the reformers had great impact on the 19th-century Indian society and culture. Reformers from different regions also became linked to the all-India nationalist movement, and reform acquired a nationalist flavour and an all-India extension. The reform movements of the 19th-century were able to achieve the following:

### Debate And Discussion

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//d2c4910f-5a20-4f60-bf37-cc335016735c/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_344_885_637_989.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A50Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa4f0cbed2aab59f13a11eec869e07270452e444ae550d31c95409d9949cc5bbf" alt="Image" width="24%" /></div>

• communication

• information literacy: general awareness

What positive changes have come about in the lives of Indian women since the reform movements of the 19th and 20th centuries?

Emancipation of women was initiated.

Widow Remarriage Act was passed in 1856.

Sati and female infanticide were banned

Education of girls was popularised.

Marriageable age of girls was raised.

The caste system became less rigid.

Western education was adopted.

The period of reform movements also witnessed considerable development in literature. Many educated Indians took to expressing their ideas and opinions in newspapers, magazines or books as poems, stories or essays. They did not write in English alone, but in their own regional languages as well. Some famous literary figures of this period were Bankim Chandra Chattopadhyay, Sarojini Naidu, Tarabai Shinde and Subramania Bharati.

Art and theatre were also arenas for the expression of India's past heritage and the need for social change. Artists such as Abanindranath Tagore and Raja Ravi Verma developed a style of art which saw a fusion of Indian artistic tradition with European techniques of painting. Therefore, the 19th-century in India was a period of social and cultural revival and regeneration.

### KEYWORDS

Brahmo Samaj: set up by Raja Ram Mohan Roy to promote liberal and modern ideas of the West Home Rule Movement: political movement launched by Annie Besant; it demanded self-rule for Indians

Ramakrishna Mission: founded by Swami Vivekananda to promote the teachings of Ramakrishna Paramahamsa

Sati: a custom in which a Hindu widow burnt herself on the funeral pyre of her husband

## 11 The Rise of Indian Nationalism

#### History Alive!

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f4248be0-acf0-46a1-baac-7ba15fc7dac1/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_130_288_753_638.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F5d9f709ef87bcbb8dd789f391f0584cd37c7ea6e34b2c2653e4f29ebdc6993fb" alt="Image" width="52%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f4248be0-acf0-46a1-baac-7ba15fc7dac1/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_828_209_960_278.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb206324643d3353dca0c02009d91542ceccc22971f83ea13e27adb0a33bf1b66" alt="Image" width="11%" /></div>

The Delhi Durbar of 1877 was held to proclaim Queen Victoria as the Empress of India. It was held with great pomp and show. Many local rulers attended the event in their finery.

An illustration depicting the

Revolt of 1857

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f4248be0-acf0-46a1-baac-7ba15fc7dac1/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_547_189_736_478.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2Fc155fbeb9a1f86352a3e6cb922634d40d2ad75144766dfc85bc0c35e8dede4bb" alt="Image" width="15%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//f4248be0-acf0-46a1-baac-7ba15fc7dac1/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_861_201_1045_469.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F60b91bf9b93608a0cf7f52f715d85e779bffa59a39fc1506de632e319f0ed3a5" alt="Image" width="15%" /></div>

The term ‘nationalism’ basically signifies a great love for one’s motherland and the desire to liberate it from foreign rule. The end of the 19th century and the beginning of the 20th century witnessed the rise of nationalist feelings among many Indians. These feelings ultimately led to the birth of the Indian national movement.

### FACTORS THAT LED TO THE RISE OF NATIONALISM

Queen Elizabeth I

Let us read about the factors that led to the rise of nationalism.

##### Revolt of 1857

Even though the revolt failed in its objective of expelling the British from India, it created in Indian minds the idea of unity and sacrifice for the nation.

The idea of belonging to one nation now gained ground.

Martyrs of the revolt became household names and inspired many Indians, young and old, to join the nationalist movement.

### Debate And Discussion SKI

communication

critical thinking: reasoning

Discuss in your class about the extent to which the Revolt of 1857 was responsible for the birth of nationalism in India.

##### Political Unification of India

The British conquests and policies unified India both politically and economically.

There was a centralised government with specific laws, rules and regulations for the entire country.

With political unification, the feeling of belonging to one nation became predominant among many people in India.

#### Spread of Western Education

The spread of Western education helped foster the spirit of nationalism.

The British had originally imposed Western education in order to create a class of clerks for their administration.

While the British succeeded in their objectives, Western education brought to Indian minds the modern ideas of freedom, liberty and fraternity.

The educated Indians also learnt about the success of the French Revolution and the American War of Independence, and they dreamed of a strong, united and free India. They learnt to take pride in India's glorious past and to oppose British perception of Indians as an inferior race. Many of these educated Indians rose to become leaders of the national movement.

### Familiarity with the English Language

The exposure to Western education allowed many Indians to learn the English language. It became the language of communication among educated people across the country.

Though Indians spoke different languages in their own regions, they often used English to express their views and exchange ideas with those belonging to other regions. This developed a sense of unity among different regional groups.

#### Role of the Press and Literature

The press played a very important role in arousing nationalist feelings.

A number of newspapers were published, both in English and in the vernacular languages.

Leaders of the nationalist movement used the vernacular press to spread modern ideas and national awareness. They discussed British policies and the evils of the British Raj.

The idea of democracy was also discussed in the vernacular press.

Nationalist literature, such as Bankim Chandra Chattopadhyay's Anandamath and Rabindranath Tagore's Ghare Baire, led to a cultural awakening of the people. These works acquainted Indians with their rich cultural heritage and aroused their nationalist aspirations.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//c618432b-6fd6-4bb6-9763-6dfe035f1778/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_809_376_1079_723.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A45Z%2F-1%2F%2F54a341a9e3c5b3e08ce05cdfc0b609c15efeb6f81e1beb66eb02ec4b6c54e9a8" alt="Image" width="22%" /></div>

Rabindranath Tagore

#### Did You Know?

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//c618432b-6fd6-4bb6-9763-6dfe035f1778/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_939_757_1032_871.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A46Z%2F-1%2F%2Fabf20ee079295a46a16cefea62896b77e42d473387fe344a82b629c7ac2084f6" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>

#### information literacy

In 1913, Rabindranath Tagore became the first non-European to win the Nobel Prize for Literature.

Together with Indians, European scholars such as Alexander Cunningham, William Jones and James Prinsep researched India's past and revealed its rich heritage.

Indians once again discovered the richness of Vedic philosophy, the wisdom of rulers such as Chandragupta Maurya, and the glory of the Gupta dynasty and the Mughal Empire. These rediscoveries helped Indians develop a sense of pride and self-confidence to demand freedom from the British rule.

### Improvement in Transportation and Communication

Lord Dalhousie and other British administrators took an active interest in establishing an effective system of transport and communication.

The development of roads and railways

narrowed regional barriers.

People travelled easily from one part of the country to another. They could meet and exchange ideas with each other. This made them realise that they shared common problems and that their goals were also the same.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//c618432b-6fd6-4bb6-9763-6dfe035f1778/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_46_638_569_1116.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A47Z%2F-1%2F%2F7f16993d68aa584c1999e83c30328073de29f4978384a9046841db4014415f16" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>

The Victoria Terminus, known today as the Chhatrapati Shivaji Terminus, is a UNESCO World Heritage Site and one of the earliest railway stations of India. It was built to improve the transport system in India.

### acial Discrimination by the British

The British considered the Indians to be an inferior and uncivilised race.

Indians were humiliated, looked down upon and treated with contempt.

Racial discrimination by the British was greatly resented by Indians. Certain instances of racial discrimination were as follows:

High-ranking positions in the Indian administration and government were only reserved for the British.

Indians were debarred from using railway coaches, hospitals, parks and clubs reserved exclusively for the British.

These racial policies antagonised many Indians, particularly the educated intelligentsia. It was this class that united the people against the British.

##### Repressive Policies of Lord Lytton

Lord Lytton was the Viceroy of India between 1876 and 1880. Certain acts passed by him went against the interests of the Indians and caused great agitation. Some of his repressive policies were as follows:

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//c618432b-6fd6-4bb6-9763-6dfe035f1778/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_874_716_1122_1004.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A47Z%2F-1%2F%2F6d593191687b071787023b1f096fcd0db5fe47fc31218eb14c43824e8cf85663" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>

Lord Lytton

The Delhi Durbar: In 1877, an Imperial Durbar was held at Delhi with great pomp and show to proclaim Queen Victoria as the Empress of India. This was organised at a time when south India was badly affected by a famine, and no welfare measures were forthcoming from the British. All these policies antagonised the Indians greatly and they decided to take concerted action against the British.

The Vernacular Press Act: It was enacted in 1878. According to this Act, restrictions were placed on the Indian press and printing anything anti-British was forbidden.

Arms Act: Introduced by Lord Lytton in 1878, this act stated that in order to carry arms, an Indian required a license; however, an European did not require a license for the same.

### Immediate Cause: The Ilbert Bill Controversy

Lord Ripon, who succeeded Lord Lytton as the Viceroy, tried to address some of the grievances of the Indians.

A bill, known as the Ilbert Bill, was introduced in 1883 by C.P. Ilbert, a Law Member of the Government of India.

The bill proposed that senior Indian magistrates could preside over cases involving Europeans accused of crimes in India.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//c618432b-6fd6-4bb6-9763-6dfe035f1778/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_242_966_479_1301.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A48Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd1db1ebf4ca6329362a7054997ec2b28cb9dc9dbb33e338526b0bf150edc773d" alt="Image" width="19%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">Lord Ripon</div> </div>

The Anglo-Indian officials and non-officials opposed the bill violently. Therefore, the bill had to be modified in favour of the European subjects.

This controversy convinced many Indians that they would have to fight for their rights. They decided to form an organised political body, which would protect the interests of the Indians.

## THE INDIAN NATIONAL CONGRESS: FORMATION AND OBJECTIVES

Both Indians and Europeans (who were sympathetic to the plight of Indians) felt the need for organisations and conferences which would bring together like-minded Indians and provide a platform to express their grievances against the British. In 1883, Surendranath Banerjee convened the Indian National Conference in Calcutta. It was a meeting of Indians from different parts of the country to discuss their concerns about the British government. Two years later, A.O. Hume laid the foundation of the Indian National Congress (INC) in 1885—a political organisation comprising Indians.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//c618432b-6fd6-4bb6-9763-6dfe035f1778/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_776_930_1038_1247.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A48Z%2F-1%2F%2Fbaad22f0ba542c1b8e263d203e2c625f4a859abeb6af356bc2acb23259636da1" alt="Image" width="22%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▶ Surendranath Banerjee</div> </div>

The first session of the Congress, held in Bombay, was presided over by W.C. Bonnerjee. Prominent national leaders who attended the session were Dadabhai Naoroji, Pherozeshah Mehta, Badruddin Tyabji and many others.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//c618432b-6fd6-4bb6-9763-6dfe035f1778/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_844_116_1063_369.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A49Z%2F-1%2F%2F96f37fb406da0cf5ffdbf3d381a0a664c39eb50a923126449a9fcf04d7f6af4b" alt="Image" width="18%" /></div>

This is an excerpt from A.O. Hume's poem, An Old Man's Hope.

A.O. Hume

Which lines in the poem try to rouse Indians?

Why do you think Hume says that the land and lives in India are at stake?

### Objectives of the Indian National Congress

Following were the main objectives of the Indian National Congress:

Promote friendly relations and unity among Indians living in different parts of the country, irrespective of race, caste, religion, or provinces

■ Channelise and organise public opinion in the country on British policies affecting Indians

Place popular demands before the government

Decide upon the future course of action for issues that concerned Indians

At the end of the first session, the Congress delegates reinforced their loyalty to the British. They asserted that they desired only more participation and involvement in the government.

The Indian National Congress therefore provided Indians with a common platform to express their dissatisfaction with the British government. As nationalist feelings spread and resentment of the government's policies increased, many nationalists looked to the Congress to play an active role in engaging the British on behalf of the Indians.

French Revolution: a revolutionary movement that erupted in France in 1789 and led to the end of the monarchy

Martyr: a person who is killed because of her/his religious or patriotic beliefs

## 12 The Indian National Movement: 1885–1916

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//52433adb-c113-4e2d-b49b-819dc744c587/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_137_236_1151_1521.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A44Z%2F-1%2F%2F0767792ee8ec41e74d6640534ac60e1300af2b39b44bf21956aa05e980734163" alt="Image" width="85%" /></div>

#### Before Reading

Tick (√) the pictures of the members of the Indian National Congress.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//52433adb-c113-4e2d-b49b-819dc744c587/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_106_181_305_435.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A46Z%2F-1%2F%2Fda454a8c867b44ea348d1acefc3f90d84d62fd6241d025bbaf57b40ec59bdc4b" alt="Image" width="16%" /></div>

Gopal Krishna Gokhale

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//52433adb-c113-4e2d-b49b-819dc744c587/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_477_190_672_433.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A46Z%2F-1%2F%2F8adbb497094a08684f069a8f9b54a9e596e4832e46f68bd124db5b4bb176e4d1" alt="Image" width="16%" /></div>

Lord Ripon

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//52433adb-c113-4e2d-b49b-819dc744c587/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_841_194_1036_438.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A46Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb4ab2745ba507849d3fbec672e566e8800545cd18567076317c3989c59ca86d0" alt="Image" width="16%" /></div>

Pherozeshah Mehta

The establishment of the Indian National Congress marked the beginning of an organised political movement by Indians to express their dissatisfaction with the nature of British rule in India. The Indian National Congress, with delegates from different parts of the country, became the mouthpiece for the politically aware Indians.

##### THE MODERATES

When the Indian National Congress was founded in 1885, it was dominated by leaders who have been described as moderates. They believed in the benevolent nature of British rule. They felt that the Indians were still not ready to govern themselves. They firmly believed that the British could be persuaded to introduce reforms for the benefit of Indians.

##### Leaders of the Moderates

Many of the moderate leaders came from educated middle class background, well-versed in Western thoughts and ideas. These leaders were teachers, lawyers, journalists and industrialists. The popular

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//52433adb-c113-4e2d-b49b-819dc744c587/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_578_527_1099_863.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A46Z%2F-1%2F%2F3f3ad59d1c97476f765299d080b81fe35e0d9968c991beecd00b1cdc75721314" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>

▶ A photograph showing the delegates of the first Indian National Congress at Bombay in 1885

moderate leaders were Dadabhai Naoroji, Surendranath Banerjee, Pherozeshah Mehta, Gopal Krishna Gokhale and many other eminent leaders.

##### Method of Approach

The moderates did not believe in the use of violence. They had faith in the British sense of fair play and justice. They therefore adopted the method of prayer, petition and protest.

The moderates presented their requirements through resolutions and petitions. They believed that the government would eventually pass laws to address these grievances.

The Indian National Movement: 1885-1916

To spread the message of unity and political awareness, they distributed pamphlets, gave lectures and wrote articles in newspapers and journals.

The moderates organised processions and protest marches. They also sent delegations to England to negotiate with the government to introduce necessary reforms in India.

##### Demands of the Moderates

The demands of the moderates were aimed at remedying the oppressive aspects in British governance. Some of their demands were as follows:

☑ Reduction of high taxes

Holding the Indian Civil Service (ICS)

examinations simultaneously in India

and England

Appointment of Indians to high posts in the administration

Reduction in military expenditure

■ Changes in British economic policies to benefit Indians

### Successes and Failures of the Moderates

The moderates have been criticised by many as they did not achieve many of their objectives. They have also been criticised as a ‘microscopic minority’—leaders who represented only a small section of the population, while the masses at large remained unaffected by their activities. Despite the criticisms levelled at the moderates, they achieved the following:

■ Due to the spread of a national consciousness among a wider section of society, people began to believe that they belonged to one nation.

Due to their efforts, more Indians became aware of the concepts of freedom, secularism and democracy.

The moderates also supported social change and spoke about reforming social evils, such as the rigid caste structure, that divided Indian society.

### RADICAL NATIONALISTS

The failure of the moderates to coax the British government into making real policy changes created dissatisfaction within the Congress. A group of Congress members who were impatient with the moderate methods of protest emerged as new leaders of the Congress. Often referred to as the radical nationalists, they played a more dominant role in the Congress activities from 1905 onwards. The radical nationalists felt that the moderate approach had proved ineffective and that more aggressive methods were necessary.

The radical leadership consisted of aggressive leaders such as Lala Lajpat Rai, Bal Gangadhar Tilak and Bipin Chandra Pal. This trio was popularly known as Lal-Bal-Pal.

#### Beliefs of the Radical Nationalists

The radicals had no faith in the British sense of justice and fair play. They felt that the British had no honest intentions of working for the welfare of the Indian people.

They believed that the British rule had done more harm to India than good.

They demanded complete independence or Swaraj and not self-government within the British Empire.

### Method of Approach

The radical method of approach included aggressive and organised political agitation, which involved the masses.

They were willing to make sacrifices, even when it involved the use of violence, if necessary.

#### Achievements

The radicals felt that the economic interest of the British government to monopolise the Indian markets had harmed Indian industries and artisans. Thus, they promoted the use of goods made in India to revive the declining Indian economy.

The radical nationalists broadened the social base of the movement by involving the masses in their activities.

### Debate And Discussion

How were the moderates and the radicals different in their approaches and methods of operation?

##### PARTITION OF BENGAL

The belief of the radicals in the oppressive nature of the British rule was further strengthened when the government decided to partition Bengal. The British Viceroy of India, Lord Curzon, was responsible for partitioning Bengal. The official reason given by Curzon was that Bengal was a very large province to be administered effectively. Therefore, Bengal needed to be partitioned to enable competent administration. But the real reason for partitioning Bengal was to drive a wedge between the Hindus and Muslims and thereby weaken the national movement. Thus, Bengal was formally partitioned on 16 October 1905 into East Bengal and West Bengal.

##### Connecting Past with Present

Then The partition of Bengal was announced to apparently improve the economic condition of

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//52433adb-c113-4e2d-b49b-819dc744c587/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_32_1056_213_1369.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A48Z%2F-1%2F%2F2d73166e62e2d4e31c7754c16003e83d0076686988545872a229e1e0aed373e3" alt="Image" width="15%" /></div>

Lord Curzon

eastern Bengal. As Calcutta was the centre of most economic and educational activities, the eastern region of Bengal and the city of Dhaka were neglected. In 1904, Lord Curzon laid the foundation stone for Curzon Hall, which was meant to be a town hall in Dhaka.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//52433adb-c113-4e2d-b49b-819dc744c587/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_seal_box_669_900_755_1007.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A48Z%2F-1%2F%2F1d3596a9c119ab1af412e31e13f1600cfa4c76a7c3ed88555d65ef4995cc4083" alt="Image" width="7%" />  <div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//52433adb-c113-4e2d-b49b-819dc744c587/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_seal_box_669_900_755_1007.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A48Z%2F-1%2F%2F1d3596a9c119ab1af412e31e13f1600cfa4c76a7c3ed88555d65ef4995cc4083" alt="Image" width="7%" />  21st CENTURY SKILLS  </div>   </div>

##### initiative and self-direction: research

Now Although the partition of Bengal was stalled temporarily, Dhaka became the capital of East Pakistan after the Partition of India in 1947. Presently, Dhaka is the capital of the independent

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//52433adb-c113-4e2d-b49b-819dc744c587/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_876_1007_1151_1228.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A48Z%2F-1%2F%2F5dee5e0a868ff444be1b7fb5797bdf73dceb045b23c792b4875b5293f01cb2a5" alt="Image" width="23%" /></div>

The Indian National Movement: 1885-1916

### THE SWADESHI AND BOYCOTT MOVEMENTS

Following the partition of Bengal, the radical nationalists launched the Swadeshi and Boycott movements against the British.

The Swadeshi Movement urged people to use only those goods that were produced by Indian manufacturers.

The Boycott Movement asked people to abstain from purchasing British or foreign goods. It also appealed to Indians to refrain from sending their children to British schools and colleges.

As protests against the partition continued, the differences between the radicals and the moderates became so great that the radicals were expelled from the Congress.

Many of the radical nationalists adopted more revolutionary methods to protest against the partition and British injustice.

These radical nationalists were joined by patriotic young men, and at times women, who were willing to employ aggressive methods to force the British to leave India.

These revolutionaries

underground (secret) societies, which

were located in different parts of the

country.

The main centres of revolutionary activities were Bengal, Maharashtra, Uttar Pradesh and Punjab.

The revolutionaries published newspapers, which strongly opposed the British rule in India. They collected weapons, manufactured bombs and planned several attacks against British officials and government buildings.

The government retaliated harshly. Many of the revolutionaries were tracked down and captured. Their hideouts were destroyed. Some of them, such as Khudiram Bose, were hanged. Others, such as Barin Ghosh and

#### Comparative History

##### Russo-Japanese War

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fc329b8e-9070-458c-a080-a8ecb0ab0a99/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_674_955_761_1062.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F8d1a9a71d1a9faeca4a8816470cbd85acd3c1ac64a3f8e88fd7e310044f1f774" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>

The Russo-Japanese War was a conflict between Russia and Japan. It happened because of the rivalry between these countries for supremacy in Manchuria and Korea. This war began in 1904 and ended in 1905. It was fought mostly on the Liaodong Peninsula (a peninsula in Liaoning Province of Northeast China), Mukden (now known as Shenyang, located in northeast China) and the Yellow Sea (located between mainland China and the Korean peninsula). Japan won this war and became the first Asian power in the modern era to defeat a European power.

##### • information literacy: comparative analysis

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fc329b8e-9070-458c-a080-a8ecb0ab0a99/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_822_1030_1116_1504.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F13381e7a16d6772227c6978562cd6ef18d198b9735bb40e7fd341f5525250d43" alt="Image" width="24%" /></div>

Hemchandra Kanungo, were imprisoned in the Andaman and Nicobar Islands.

Despite such stern measures, nationalist Indians continued their protest of the British rule in India.

#### Surat Split

Due to the differences in their beliefs and methods, a split occurred between the moderates and the radicals at Surat session of the Indian National Congress in 1907.

In 1911, Bengal was reunited. However, the capital of the country was shifted from Calcutta to Delhi.

### FORMATION OF THE ALL INDIA MUSLIM LEAGUE

Apart from the Congress, other communities in India also came together to form political organisations and promote nationalism. In 1906, a Muslim deputation met Viceroy Lord Minto. The deputation requested for separate representation and an organisation for the Muslims.

The British government willingly accepted the requests of the deputation, and Lord Minto

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fc329b8e-9070-458c-a080-a8ecb0ab0a99/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_6_1154_80_1612.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F74744632fcc0342541d3bcfc929d7143bd77419f4ae2d38ef139f55224cf938b" alt="Image" width="6%" /></div>

##### Did You Know?

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fc329b8e-9070-458c-a080-a8ecb0ab0a99/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_307_1131_585_1232.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe2acb10b42bb27147ebebd88b579257de56f6aab03e05f6bba943a1514a3e42d" alt="Image" width="23%" /></div>

Mohammed Ali Jinnah joined the All India Muslim League in 1913. He served as a leader of the All India Muslim League till 1947. He became the first Governor-General of Pakistan on 14 August 1947. He is officially known in Pakistan as Quaid-e-Azam.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fc329b8e-9070-458c-a080-a8ecb0ab0a99/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_370_1219_562_1459.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe2a9c8b95ea868c3c89fac7a91f3e55f8446fbfcf49fa7017e2e482e213cca93" alt="Image" width="16%" /></div>

Mohammed Ali

Jinnah

assured them about separate representation. By the initiative of Nawab Salimullah of Dacca (now Dhaka), the All India Muslim League was formally founded during a public meeting of muslim leaders in 1906.

### Aims of the All India Muslim League

The formation of the All India Muslim League was welcomed by the British. The government felt that separate political organisations for the Hindus and Muslims would prevent the two religious communities from coming together and uniting against the British.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fc329b8e-9070-458c-a080-a8ecb0ab0a99/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_588_617_1095_914.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd25857fc95da43492910e6f06911fe8f00947c275138db6a17288b8870a6bec3" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">► Leaders of the Muslim League</div> </div>

The aims of the All India Muslim League were to:

promote among the Muslims a feeling of loyalty towards the British government.

protect and promote the political rights of the Muslims.

provide a political platform for the upper-class Muslims.

#### THE INDIAN COUNCIL ACT, 1909

In 1909, the British government passed the Indian Council Act, popularly known as the Morley-Minto Reforms. It was named after the Viceroy, Lord Minto and the Secretary of State, John Morley.

Keeping in mind the assurances given to the Muslim League, Lord Minto granted separate electorates. This proved beneficial not only for the Muslims, but also for the British, as it sought to keep the Hindus and the Muslims divided. According to the system of separate electorates, the Hindus could vote only for Hindus and the Muslims could vote only for Muslims.

### TRENDS IN THE NATIONALIST MOVEMENT TILL 1916

In 1916, the Muslim League changed its objective from loyalty to the British rule to demand for self-government within the British Empire. The Muslims of India were disappointed over the British support of the abolition of the Ottoman Empire. The sultan of the Ottoman Empire was also the caliph—the religious head of the worldwide Muslim community. The Muslims perceived this decision as disrespectful of their religious sentiments, and their faith in the British government was shaken.

With this common objective, both the Congress and the Muslim League held their annual session at Lucknow in 1916, and the famous Lucknow Pact was signed. The Lucknow Pact was important for the following reasons:

The Hindus and Muslims were united once again after the partition of Bengal.

The radical nationalists were brought back within the fold of the Congress, thus strengthening the national movement.

Another important event in the history of the Indian national movement was the foundation of the Home Rule League.

It was organised by Annie Besant and Bal Gangadhar Tilak in 1916.

The movement was started to demand Swaraj or self-government.

It succeeded in arousing the masses, revived the Swadeshi spirit and forced the British government to make certain administrative changes.

#### After Reading

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fc329b8e-9070-458c-a080-a8ecb0ab0a99/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_24_1024_1155_1609.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2Fc77abff29b49b5dd8a79c1a86fab4b1cd2c552762f85e2235ddae354b61f1a15" alt="Image" width="95%" /></div>

### KEYWORDS

Boycott: to abstain from the purchase of British or foreign goods and refrain from going to British schools or colleges

Moderates: the leaders who led the Indian national movement in the early years and believed in petition, prayer and protest as the means of agitation

Radical nationalists: the leaders of the national movement who believed in aggressive methods of opposition to the British government

Separate electorates: division of the voting population of the country into separate electorates based on religion, region or caste; the Hindus could vote only for Hindus and the Muslims could vote only for Muslims

Swadeshi: the use of goods that are produced in the country itself

Swaraj: complete independence

1. Tick (✓) the correct option.

Nautanki on Swadeshi and Boycott Movements

creativity: imagination

collaboration

communication

Nautanki is a folk operatic $ ^{*} $ theatre form, performed in northern parts of India. Central to the performance is a percussion instrument, such as a drum, that is beaten to gather the audience together and at opportune moments in the play.

With the help of your drama teacher, write a nautanki on the events leading up to the Swadeshi and Boycott Movements. Choose rhyming words for your dialogues. Conclude the nautanki showing the various ways in which protests were carried out against the British in these movements. Enact this as a street play in your school campus.

*operative: related to a drama in which participants often sing the dialogues accompanied by music

## Mahatma Gandhi and the Indian National Movement: 1917 – 1947

##### History Alive!

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//30c94f0b-a8fa-4dfb-8ec1-c148dd2c5a50/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_1005_233_1125_305.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A53Z%2F-1%2F%2F4de7fe67f3b753b11dcb975e721876f5655fcf2cc7c95a76a79f8cc4d6e8b375" alt="Image" width="10%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//30c94f0b-a8fa-4dfb-8ec1-c148dd2c5a50/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_179_307_749_702.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A53Z%2F-1%2F%2F6913c0a13ed914038f79f3031ef2dfe72a976102b55de2ebbd18f28c235047b7" alt="Image" width="47%" /></div>

In 1930, Mahatma Gandhi, along with some of his followers, marched from Sabarmati Ashram to the coastal town of Dandi. His Dandi March marked the beginning of the Civil Disobedience Movement.

##### Learning Outcomes

At the end of this lesson, learners will be able to:

assess the Gandhian Era (1917-1947) of the Indian National Movement.

outline the early campaigns at Kheda, Champaran and Ahmedabad.

discuss the causes, withdrawal and impact of the Non-cooperation Movement.

evaluate the causes of the Civil Disobedience Movement.

analyse the events leading to Indian independence and partition.

trace the developments that led to the Quit India Movement.

highlight the role played by Subhas Chandra Bose and the INA.

Members of the Cabinet

Mission to India meeting

Mohammed Ali Jinnah

The Second Round Table Conference

M ohandas Karamchand Gandhi, popularly known as Mahatma Gandhi or Gandhiji, was born on 2 October 1869 at Porbandar in Gujarat. After his early education in India, he went to England to study law. Thereafter, in 1893, he went to South Africa to practise as a barrister. In South Africa, Gandhi was shocked and enraged at the racial discrimination and oppression meted out by the British colonists to the non-White people. He decided to fight against such injustice.

During Gandhi's stay in South Africa, he evolved the concept of satyagraha (devotion to the truth), based on the principles of truth and non-violence—a concept that he later applied to the Indian national movement.

##### THE CONCEPT OF SATYAGRAHA

Gandhi believed that a person should firmly believe in truth and non-violence and resist evil to follow the principles of satyagraha. A satyagrahi must be fearless and strong and oppose evil actions. He must be willing to make sacrifices and accept suffering.

During the fight for India's freedom from the British rule, Gandhi followed certain methods of protest based on satyagraha. They were as follows:

Peaceful demonstrations

Defiance of unjust British laws

Boycott of British goods and services

Non-payment of oppressive taxes

Promotion of the swadeshi spirit through the use of  $ \underline{\text{charkha}} $ and homespun khadi

##### Early Experiments with

##### Satyagraha

■ Gandhi's first experiment with satyagraha in India was at Champaran (1917) in Bihar. Here he took up the cause of the indigo cultivators against the planters. He launched a movement which forced the government to reduce the rent the Indian peasants were required to pay to the European planters.

After his success at Champaran, Gandhi took up the cause of the peasants of

Kheda in Gujarat in 1918. Gandhi was successful in ensuring the suspension of tax collection for a year because the crops had failed.

In 1918, Gandhi also fought for the textile mill workers of Ahmedabad. He was successful in raising the wages of the workers.

With these early experiments in satyagraha, Gandhi won over popular leaders of the national movement. In Bihar, Dr Rajendra Prasad, and in Gujarat, Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel, became enthusiastic and staunch supporters of Gandhi's methods of protest.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fd2b56c5-8ab2-4fd0-9727-424b89dbece3/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_81_593_345_954.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F2277b62948d5d6fb6272f0231d2e51ae7cf352a060c5c74ca7f42af13f01477f" alt="Image" width="22%" /></div>

Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fd2b56c5-8ab2-4fd0-9727-424b89dbece3/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_348_595_615_956.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F98c7330e229f9f5b6cfbaff31e710deccd77897e7e72c198a485b3479f8288b5" alt="Image" width="22%" /></div>

► Rajendra Prasad

##### GANDHI'S VISIONS

Mahatma Gandhi’s emphasis on Hindu–Muslim unity and social justice was another key aspect of his methods for achieving India’s independence.

##### Hindu-Muslim Unity

Gandhi wrote, ‘Indian culture... is neither Hindu, Islamic nor any other, wholly. It is a fusion of all.’ According to him, the path to freedom in India lay in Hindu–Muslim unity and he worked tirelessly towards it.

##### Social Justice

Mahatma Gandhi believed in justice for all—including the poor and downtrodden. He fought to improve the condition of the lower castes and the attitude towards women. He called the people of the lower castes the Harijans or 'the children of God'.

After Gandhi returned to India in 1915, he studied the condition of the Indian national movement closely. He realised that Hindu-Muslim relations were strained and the lower classes were barely a part of the movement. He toured the entire country and came to the conclusion that without the support of the masses, no struggle for independence could be successful. So, he organised regional movements with peasants and workers to create a popular base for the national movement.

### THE NON-COOPERATION MOVEMENT (1920–22)

The Non-cooperation Movement was one of the earliest attempts by Gandhi to bring together all Indians and force the British to grant self-government to India. The causes for the launch of this movement are explained below.

##### Rowlatt Act

The Rowlatt Act was passed in March 1919. It was also known as the Black Act as it curtailed the freedom of the Indian people. The clauses of the Act were as follows:

To carry out arrests without a warrant

To conduct the trials of certain political cases without a jury

Imprisonment for an indefinite period

This act created discontentment and anger against the injustice of the British rule. The government, unable to control the situation, used severely repressive methods. At this point, on 6 April 1919, Gandhi called for a day of national fasting, meetings and suspension of work as an act of satyagraha to protest against the Rowlatt Act.

### Jallianwala Bagh Massacre

On 13 April 1919, a public meeting was called at Jallianwala Bagh in Amritsar to protest against the measures of the Rowlatt Act. The meeting was peaceful and the people were unarmed. However, General Dyer, the British military commander, had issued an order banning all public meetings and hartals. He surrounded the Bagh with his troops, blocking its only exit, and opened fire on the gathering. There was no warning, and the shooting continued till the troops ran out of ammunition. Hundreds were killed and thousands wounded.

This massacre of innocent people was condemned by all Indians. There were severe protests all over the country. Rabindranath Tagore gave up his knighthood in protest. Martial law was declared in Punjab. Gandhi lost all faith in the British government's claim to fair play and justice. He urged people not to believe or cooperate with such a government.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fd2b56c5-8ab2-4fd0-9727-424b89dbece3/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_22_1177_505_1546.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F30a894c587186d02ce1ea56a9725d613551ab792f12fa13c2f81eb7789235475" alt="Image" width="40%" /></div>

After the Jallianwala Bagh Massacre, Gandhi launched the Non-cooperation Movement in 1920.

The methods of resistance adopted by Gandhi were as follows:

Boycott of legislative councils, law courts and government schools and colleges

Surrender of titles and honorary posts awarded by the British

Promotion of Hindu-Muslim unity

Promotion of swadeshi goods and the boycott of foreign goods

Boycott of government functions and elections

The use of khadi gained popularity among all people, including the upper classes. The charkha, or the spinning wheel, became the symbol of the Non-cooperation Movement.

The Non-cooperation Movement was the first large-scale mass movement organised by Gandhi. Many sections of society were drawn into it. The Congress was transformed from a ‘microscopic minority’ into a mass-based party. Hindu–Muslim unity was negotiated. The movement, by supporting the Khilafat Movement, included Muslims in the fight for freedom from British domination.

When the movement was at its peak, violence erupted in 1922 at Chauri Chaura—a small town in the district of Gorakhpur in Uttar Pradesh. The police fired at a peaceful procession. The angry mob retaliated and burnt down the police station, killing some policemen. Gandhi disapproved this violence and immediately called off the movement.

##### Did You Know?

In 1919, Muslims in British India launched a pan-Islamic political protest campaign. Known as the Khilafat Movement, it was led by the Ali brothers—Muhammad Ali and Shaukat Ali. The Ali brothers began the movement to protest against the abolition of the office of the Caliph in Turkey.

### THE CIVIL DISOBEDIENCE MOVEMENT (1930–34)

The Civil Disobedience Movement launched by Gandhi and the Congress in 1930 also followed the method of satyagraha. The events led to this movement are discussed as follows.

### Reaction against the Simon Commission

In 1927, a commission headed by Sir John Simon was sent by the British government to review its functioning in India. It came to be known as the Simon Commission.

From the outset, the Simon Commission was boycotted by the Indians, mainly because it was an all-White commission. It had no Indian member to represent India. The recommendations of the Simon Commission were also not acceptable to the national leaders.

##### Poorna Swaraj Resolution

The Congress held its annual session at Lahore in December 1929. Jawaharlal Nehru was the President at this session of the Congress. In this session, the resolution of Poorna Swaraj, or complete independence, was adopted. The decision to boycott the First Round Table Conference in London and declare 26 January 1930 as Independence Day for India were also taken. The Indian tricolour was adopted and unfurled, and people all over the country took the pledge of freedom. The Congress also decided to launch a Civil Disobedience Movement under Gandhi's leadership.

In March 1930, Gandhi launched the Civil Disobedience Movement with the Salt Satyagraha. The British government had established its monopoly over salt, a necessary item in every household. Indians were forced to pay tax on salt and were not allowed to manufacture it.

##### Dandi March

Gandhi undertook the historic and famous Dandi March to protest against the salt laws. He marched from the Sabarmati Ashram to Dandi—a village on the coast of Gujarat—to break these laws. He was joined by thousands of people on the way.

#### Analysing Primary Sources

This is a photograph of a protest by Indians during the Non-cooperation Movement.

What do you observe in the picture?

Do you think the picture tells you about the method of protest followed by the nationalists?

Do you think the method was in tune with Gandhi's idea of satyagraha?

▶ Non-cooperation Movement

On reaching Dandi, Gandhi picked up a handful of salt from the beach to break the salt laws. This symbolic action was imitated all over India, and people began to manufacture and sell salt openly.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fd2b56c5-8ab2-4fd0-9727-424b89dbece3/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_100_250_502_818.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2Ffd82de38d30fb43dcc5ea319f18103c07dd234c95fec8e3550a59cc2bd88ee8c" alt="Image" width="33%" /></div>

► Gandhi picking up a handful of salt at the end of Dandi March

The Civil Disobedience Movement became an all-India mass movement. Strikes, hartals, boycott of government offices, schools and colleges brought life to a standstill. People defied the British authorities fearlessly. They refused to pay taxes or buy foreign goods. A significant aspect of the movement was that it was truly non-violent in nature. Women too participated in this movement.

##### Government Repression

The government came down with severe repressive measures, but this did not deter the people. Important leaders, including Jawaharlal Nehru and Gandhi, were arrested, thousands of Indians were imprisoned and

hundreds were injured and even killed in lathi-charge and police firing. Nationalist feelings and aspirations were strong at this point. The British realised that tangible reforms were necessary to pacify the Indians.

##### Gandhi-Irwin Pact

Realising that a dialogue with the Indian leaders had become necessary, the Viceroy Lord Irwin signed a pact with Gandhi, known as the Gandhi-Irwin Pact. According to this pact, Gandhi agreed to suspend the Civil Disobedience Movement and attend the Second Round Table Conference. Lord Irwin, on his part, agreed to release all prisoners and permit people to manufacture salt.

### The Second Round Table Conference and Relevance of Civil Disobedience Movement

The Second Round Table Conference was held between September and December 1931. Gandhi was chosen as the sole representative of the Congress. At the Conference, there was no discussion of granting the rights of self-governance to Indians. Gandhi returned empty-handed and relaunched the Civil Disobedience Movement.

The Civil Disobedience Movement made it clear to the British that certain tangible constitutional reforms would have to be granted to the Indians. The failure of the Round Table Conferences had further strengthened this idea. As a result, the British passed the Government of India Act in 1935.

##### Government of India Act, 1935

Political activity in India intensified after the Government of India Act, 1935. Elections were held in 1937. While both the Congress and the Muslim League decided to contest the elections, the Indian National Congress won by a huge margin.

When World War II broke out in 1939, Britain realised the need for Indian support to fight the war. Nationalist leaders of India were willing to help Britain, provided India was made independent. This led to a deadlock between the British government and the Indian nationalist leaders.

##### Cripps Mission

The Cripps Mission, led by Sir Stafford Cripps, was sent in 1942 to resolve the deadlock. The main proposals of the Cripps Mission were as follows:

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fd2b56c5-8ab2-4fd0-9727-424b89dbece3/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_341_676_611_990.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F3343b550a37e47ef6a00db9b47e1b177e22a2f4e327aaa31078cb0620c15009e" alt="Image" width="22%" /></div>

Sir Stafford Cripps

India would be given ‘dominion status’ after the war.

The provinces or princely states would have the right to join the Indian Dominion or remain outside it.

Gandhi rejected the proposals of the Cripps Mission by calling it a 'post-dated cheque'. He felt that the proposals offered were 'too little and too late'. He realised that the British government was not prepared to transfer any effective power to the Indians.

##### QUIT INDIA MOVEMENT

The Congress resolved to launch the Quit India Movement in August 1942. Gandhi gave the slogan 'Do or Die', which inspired the entire nation. But even before the movement could begin, all the leaders, including Gandhi, were arrested and the Congress was banned.

### Features of the Quit India Movement

People reacted spontaneously. Even without the leaders, protest marches, demonstrations and strikes were

#### Comparative History

##### The Great Depression

The Great Depression, a worldwide economic slump, started in 1929 and lasted until about 1939. It originated in the United States after the stock market crash. It was the longest and worst economic depression in the history of the industrialised world. The Depression caused large-scale unemployment, loss of production and poverty across the globe.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//fd2b56c5-8ab2-4fd0-9727-424b89dbece3/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_683_1046_1134_1524.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F95bbb673a97743900e703eb8f4df13db38992974f7199b424b0d455e0eb050b7" alt="Image" width="37%" /></div>

Unemployed men standing in a queue outside a soup kitchen during the Great Depression in Chicago

organised. The government tried to control the situation with lathi-charge and firing.

Enraged by the government's brutality, people attacked government offices, buildings, railway stations and police stations.

Telegraph lines were damaged and cut. People attacked railway lines and mangled the tracks, disrupting the network lines. The government responded by calling out the army. Thousands were killed and the movement was suppressed.

The Quit India Movement was an important landmark in India's struggle for freedom. The people acquired new confidence to fight against the British Raj. The Indians were very clear in their demand—complete independence and not dominion status. To protest against the British authority, parallel governments were set up in Ballia in Uttar Pradesh and Midnapore in Bengal. The Quit India Movement was crucial in uniting the people of India. By the end of World War II, Britain could no longer ignore the demand for India's independence.

### INDIAN NATIONAL ARMY AND SUBHAS CHANDRA BOSE

Subhas Chandra Bose, also known as Netaji, was a very important leader of the Indian national movement. He entered politics at an early age and aggressively fought for Swaraj. He became the Congress President twice—1938 and 1939. When differences arose between him and Gandhi, Bose resigned from the presidentship of the Congress.

Subhas Chandra Bose formed the Forward Bloc in 1939. The main objectives of the Forward Bloc were to get freedom from the British Rule in the immediate future and to promote national unity. When the British declared war against the Axis powers on India's behalf, Bose organised a mass protest in Calcutta. He was imprisoned and then kept under house arrest, from where he escaped to Berlin and later to Japan.

#### Connecting Past with Present

Then In September 1942, Captain Mohan Singh brought together 40,000 Indian soldiers to form the Azad Hind Fauj or the INA. When Subhas Chandra Bose was asked to take up the supreme command of the INA, he agreed to do so. In July 1943, he took the salute of the INA and was greeted as Netaji or the 'leader'.

After becoming the leader of the Azad Hind Fauj, or the Indian National Army (INA), in 1943, Netaji took an oath to free India. He gave the slogan, 'Give me blood and I will give you freedom'. Netaji's inspiring, patriotic speeches motivated the soldiers of the Azad Hind Fauj to lay down their lives fighting to free the country.

One cannot dismiss the contribution of the INA to India's freedom struggle. The INA, along with its leader, Netaji, contributed heroically to the freedom movement. Subhas Chandra Bose became an icon for future generations, and is remembered today for his patriotism and heroism.

In 1943, Subhas Chandra Bose announced the formation of the Provisional Government of Free India in Singapore and declared war on the allies. He then went to Tokyo to seek help from Japan. He was received with full honours, as would be due to the head of any country.

### Role of the INA: Achievements and Failures

The INA along with the Japanese army crossed many territories including Burma to finally reach India. In 1944, they captured Kohima, reached Imphal and planted the Indian tricolour flag there. However, the victories of the INA were short-lived. The Japanese and INA forces were defeated in a counteroffensive by the British who regained control of Burma. The INA lost its momentum

### EVENTS LEADING TOWARDS INDEPENDENCE

In 1945, the Labour Party, under Clement Attlee, came to power in Britain.

#### Cabinet Mission Plan (1946)

The Cabinet Mission was constituted at the initiative of Clement Attlee to plan the transfer of power from the British government to the Indian leadership.

Jawaharlal Nehru was invited to form the Interim Government in 1946. Jinnah stressed on his demand for Pakistan and launched

<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">Lord and Lady Mountbatten with Mahatma Gandhi</div> </div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5864911e-c9eb-4b71-8705-f329962754db/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_551_1052_1125_1542.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2Fcff597348d1ebba9f3815b80b3850c1ecd28fba4c90b0e3d82c6da00a82af159" alt="Image" width="48%" /></div>

the Direct Action Day on 16 August 1946. Direct Action Day was followed by communal violence all over the country.

##### Partition of India

Lord Mountbatten, India's last Viceroy, arrived in March 1947. He realised the need to immediately put an end to the widespread violence. The Partition of India was seen as a solution to this problem. Thus, after several meetings with leaders of the Congress and the Muslim League, it was finally decided by the Mountbatten Plan that India would be divided into two separate dominions—India and Pakistan. The Indian political leaders accepted the division. Following the passing of the Indian Independence Act of 1947, two independent nations were born.

The main provisions of this Act were as follows:

Two independent dominions—India and Pakistan—were created. The territories of these dominions were defined.

The Act provided for the appointment of a Governor-General for each dominion. Lord Mountbatten became the first Governor-General of India and

### Debate SKILLS And Discussion

Imagine you are one of the leaders of Indian National Movement. Based on the reading of this chapter, briefly discuss your method of struggle and your vision of a free India.

Mohammed Ali Jinnah became the first Governor-General of Pakistan.

With effect from 15 August 1947, the British Government would cease to have any responsibility for the Government of India.

The office of the Secretary of State was to be abolished.

The tricolour was unfurled at the Red Fort on 15 August 1947 and Jawaharlal Nehru became the first Prime Minister of independent India.

Despite the Partition, communal violence continued to occur along India's border with Pakistan. Finally, Gandhi undertook a fast unto death to put an end to this violence. On 26 January 1950, India adopted the Constitution and was declared a sovereign, socialist, secular, democratic republic.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//5864911e-c9eb-4b71-8705-f329962754db/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_65_1109_1157_1500.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F61b8947d52998ad4817aebeecaf0d3862640a5bb05ee2fbff5f1286e295ed197" alt="Image" width="91%" /></div>

#### KEY WORDS

Axis powers: the nations, namely Germany, Japan and Italy, that fought in World War II against the Allied powers constituting France, Poland, Great Britain, the USA and the Soviet Union

Civil Disobedience Movement: launched in 1930 to protest against unjust laws; involved disobeying laws and boycotting British goods, services and institutions

Dandi March: symbolised the launch of the Civil Disobedience Movement—Gandhi marched from Sabarmati to Dandi to break the salt laws

.Jans: means the 'children of God'; the name given by Gandhi to the untouchable castes Hartal: a strike in protest of something

Indian Independence Act: passed in July 1947 by the British Parliament to end the British rule in India

Khadi: an Indian homespun cotton cloth

Non-cooperation Movement: launched by Gandhi in 1920 for the attainment of Swaraj through peaceful means

Planters: Europeans during the British Raj who often owned indigo factories and forced peasants to grow indigo

Salt laws: included a number of acts passed by the British government which made production and possession of salt by Indians illegal; only the government could collect and manufacture salt at the salt depots in India

Satyagraha: a movement started by Gandhi based on the principles of truth and non-violence
