## 14 Organs of the Indian Government

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_29_185_1171_1684.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A43Z%2F-1%2F%2F1a400456cc765a6405e32047d56161fdd49ad5a5d3a4a55ecbdc2d1a939d9a55" alt="Image" width="95%" /></div>

Study the given pictures. Can you name these Prime Ministers of India?

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_121_174_329_428.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A44Z%2F-1%2F%2F436bdee861f4ba6c6fbab13ea47fc027c72977e98117254c0551740fd4753021" alt="Image" width="17%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_474_171_686_426.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A44Z%2F-1%2F%2F93bae5b54845072d1e551be72efc1ae74271938e6bb63d2881de749eaea3ba3e" alt="Image" width="17%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_826_169_1037_419.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A44Z%2F-1%2F%2F94183890af1d3dc4147941712d0d3478ed9c6609c35782ce2be63c1ab64caae0" alt="Image" width="17%" /></div>

India is a parliamentary democracy, where the supreme power resides with the people of the country. The Indian Constitution has declared India to be a Union of States. In India, power is distributed between the central and the state governments.

There are three organs of the government of India.

Legislature—makes laws

Judiciary—interprets the laws and checks the working of the legislature and executive

Executive—executes the laws

##### WHO MAKES OUR LAWS?

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_0_1110_75_1293.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A44Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa83d9f8e16faa82668ac03d88040e182c6572854997208e719f9b6622d5cf894" alt="Image" width="6%" /></div>

Legislature is a part of the government, which makes and amends laws. The Indian Parliament, known as the Sansad, is the law-making body at the central level. The state legislatures make laws at the state level. The legislature makes laws on subjects given in three lists—Union List, State List and Concurrent List (Refer to the table given on the next page).

Union List: It includes subjects, such as banking and defence, on which only the Centre can legislate.

State List: The state legislatures make laws on subjects given in the State List. Subjects such as agriculture and public health are the prerogative of the states.

Concurrent List: Subjects such as economic and social planning, electricity and education, which can be concerns for both the Centre and the states, are provided in this list. However, if there is a conflict between the Centre and a state over a subject in the Concurrent List, the central law will prevail.

##### THE UNION PARLIAMENT

The Parliament is a representative body, which can make or change the country's laws. The Indian Parliament consists of the Lok Sabha, the Rajya Sabha and the President.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_627_1324_1188_1501.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A44Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb8cd2f6129486eca8a82d29b9c37f587693784173d15f3ee897c24f4877d3752" alt="Image" width="47%" /></div>

<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Union List</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>State List</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Concurrent List</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Defence</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Public health, hospitals, dispensaries</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Education</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Banking</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Agriculture</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Factories and trade unions</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Railways</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Prisons</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Electricity</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Post and telegraph</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Water supply</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Prevention of cruelty to animals</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Airways and shipping</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Markets and fairs</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Forests</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Foreign affairs</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Land tenures and relations between landlords and tenants</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Population control</td></tr></table>

##### Lok Sabha

The Lok Sabha is also known as the House of the People or the Lower House.

##### Composition

The maximum strength of the Lok Sabha is 552.

Up to 530 members can be represented from the states, and not more than 20 members shall represent the Union Territories.

Two members of the Anglo-Indian community may be nominated by the President to the Lok Sabha, if she/he feels that this community is not adequately represented in the House.

The allotment of seats to various states is on the basis of population.

Seats are also reserved for the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes in the Lok Sabha.

##### Manner of Election

In India, every citizen who is above the age of 18 years has been given the right to vote without being discriminated on the basis of caste, religion and sex, under Universal Adult Suffrage.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_670_383_1166_712.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A45Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd47478455b01cad148a1e0ba7ada44af6b2ee8def2923e7184e94713941cb474" alt="Image" width="41%" /></div>

People standing in a queue to vote

Members of the Lok Sabha are directly elected on the basis of Universal Adult Suffrage.

Elections are held using the secret ballot system.

### Qualifications for Members of the Lok Sabha

Must be a citizen of India

Must not be less than 25 years of age

Must be of sound mind

Must not be bankrupt or convicted in any criminal case

##### Term of Office

The term of the Lok Sabha is five years.

The President has the power to dissolve the Lok Sabha before its term ends.

The term of the House can be extended during the Proclamation of Emergency.

### Connecting Past with Present

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_25_131_266_490.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A46Z%2F-1%2F%2F03591ab9de765322eea69d020f867da9ea266d8d8fbeea1fd73200256a21c780" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>

after Independence, the news about the proceedings of the Lok Sabha was transmitted through newspapers and radio. The radio typically broadcasted the morning and the evening Lok Sabha news.

Now One entire channel on television, known as the Lok Sabha TV, focuses completely on the affairs of the Lok Sabha.

Have you seen this channel? How do you think the media helps us to understand government affairs better?

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_878_217_1070_411.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A46Z%2F-1%2F%2F3112a17843276153f62544da5bb93cb78d394dea586ba33c79b625df9e409bf8" alt="Image" width="16%" /></div>

##### Sessions of the House

A session means a period during which the House meets to conduct business.

The two sessions of the Parliament are summoned by the President. However, 6 months must not lapse between two sessions.

The Speaker is the presiding officer of the Lok Sabha.

Lok Sabha conducts three sessions in a year, namely, the Budget Session, the Monsoon Session and the Winter Session.

##### Speaker of the Lok Sabha

■ She/He is elected by the members of the Lok Sabha.

■ The Speaker regulates debates, presides over meetings and maintains discipline in the House.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_233_1258_324_1361.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A46Z%2F-1%2F%2Faef2fdcec20d2212c9010d75f6eb74e22240ea422829bf2ec0b640e19a9dd409" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>

leadership and responsibility

As the Speaker, how would you conduct a day's proceedings of the Lok Sabha?

##### Rajya Sabha

The Rajya Sabha is also known as the Upper House or the Council of States. The presiding officer of the Rajya Sabha is the Vice President of India. She/He is the ex-officio Chairperson of the Rajya Sabha.

##### Composition

The maximum strength of the Rajya Sabha is 250 members.

The members are either nominated or elected.

The President nominates 12 members, from persons having special knowledge, or practical experience in matters, such as science, arts, literature or social services.

The Rajya Sabha has 238 elected members who are the representatives of states and union territories.

Seats in the Rajya Sabha are allocated according to the population of each state.

##### Manner of Election

The members of the Rajya Sabha are indirectly elected by the system of proportional representation, by the means of a single transferable vote system.

Qualifications and disqualifications for the members of the Rajya Sabha are the same as that of the members of the Lok Sabha. However, a candidate wishing to be a member of the Rajya Sabha must not be less than 30 years of age.

##### Term of Office

The Rajya Sabha is a permanent house.

One-third of the members retire every two years.

A member elected for a full term serves for a period of six years.

### FUNCTIONS OF THE UNION PARLIAMENT

A bill is introduced in either House of the Parliament, if it is an ordinary bill. A bill is a draft of a proposed law presented to the Parliament for discussion. However, a money bill can only be introduced in the Lok Sabha. A bill goes through three stages of reading. In the first stage, the bill is introduced in the House. In the second stage, voting on the bill takes place after the debate. Then the bill is sent to the other House, where the same procedure is followed. In case of a money bill, the Rajya Sabha is given only 14 days to consider the bill. In the third stage, the bill is sent to the President for his assent. The President can either sign the bill or send it back for reconsideration to the House, where the bill was presented. When the President signs the bill, the bill becomes an Act.

### THE EXECUTIVE STRUCTURE IN INDIA

The Union and State Legislature are entrusted with the task of making laws. Similarly, the Union and State Executives are entrusted with the task of enforcing laws throughout the country. The Executive

Giani Zail Singh

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_135_1296_277_1460.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A48Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb51d829f3e098134dc7bc55fd48289f200ee99100ff23caf7962c9b4e6fdd499" alt="Image" width="11%" /></div>

R. Venkataraman

Dr Shankar Dayal

Sharma

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_475_1303_621_1468.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A48Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd13dbe3ad5d3fbb8c157bcbea0df1ab8e81b1ba814dfba88f48c59e7ef007d63" alt="Image" width="12%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_819_1306_964_1486.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A49Z%2F-1%2F%2F13357d0c9e252d2a33aed97dec5c900331184db6fd3a075f0a7e74de4d772b9d" alt="Image" width="12%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//776bf468-5b4b-4208-ae97-d56e49380a38/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_990_1303_1119_1480.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A49Z%2F-1%2F%2F2dcbbb6c35b57a3addeceb751066513493ff002bedfca5d406fc43e49838a890" alt="Image" width="10%" /></div>

Pranab Mukherjee

includes the Prime Minister, the President, the Governor and other ministers.

There are two sets of government in India—one at the Centre and the other at the state level. At the Centre, the Executive comprises the President, the Vice President, the Prime Minister and the Council of Ministers. At the state level, the Executive comprises the Governor, the Chief Minister and the Council of Ministers.

##### President

The President or Rashtrapati is the head of the State. She/He exercises executive powers either directly or through officers. The President is also the first citizen of the country.

#### Qualifications for the Post of President

Must be a citizen of India

Must be at least 35 years of age

Should not hold an office of profit under the government—Centre, state or local level

Must be qualified to become a member of the Lok Sabha

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//7daec36b-57cc-4348-87ec-3574e9313d60/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_68_1054_585_1483.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A43Z%2F-1%2F%2F983803843b74e5319fe84f553b951254f6f95efc758a66757bbdaa3aea93302c" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>

Rashtrapati Bhavan, New Delhi

##### Election and Removal

The President is elected indirectly by an electoral college consisting of the Members of Parliament (MPs), and the Members of Legislative Assemblies (MLAs) of the states.

The President is elected for a period of five years. She/He can be re-elected for another term.

The President's office can fall vacant under the following instances:

Expiry of the term

On death of the President

☐ Resignation

□ Impeachment

##### Impeachment of President

Impeachment is a procedure outlined in our Constitution, by which the Parliament can remove the President. The President is impeached if she/he violates the Constitution, or is guilty of treason or corruption.

#### Powers and Functions of the President

The powers of the President can be grouped under the following heads:

##### Executive Powers

The President appoints the Prime Minister, who is the leader of the single largest party in the Lok Sabha or the leader of the coalition that wins the elections.

The President also appoints the Council of Ministers on the advice of the Prime Minister.

The President appoints and removes the high dignitaries of the states. They include  $ \underline{\text{Attorney General}} $, Comptroller

and Auditor General of India, Governors of states, ambassadors, members of the Finance Commission and Union Public Service Commission, Chief Election Commissioner, and Chief Commissioner's of Union Territories.

Judges of the Supreme Court and High Courts are also appointed by the President.

##### Military Powers

The President is the  $ \underline{\text{Supreme}} $ Commander of the Defence Forces.

The President has the power to declare war and conclude peace.

All important treaties are made in the name of the President.

The  $ \underline{\text{President}} $ represents (India) in international conferences.

##### Legislative Powers

The  $ \underline{\text{President summons}} $ the Parliament, and can dissolve the Lok Sabha.

No bill can become an Act without the assent of the President. In case of an ordinary bill, she/he can send it back with her/his recommendation to the House where the bill originated. In case of a money bill, she/he has to sign it in the first instance.

The President nominates two members of the Anglo-Indian community in the Lok Sabha. Moreover, 12 members to the Rajya Sabha from among persons having special knowledge in literature, arts, science and social service are also nominated by the President.

The President can issue ordinances when the Parliament is not in session. Ordinances are temporary laws passed by the President. They have the force of law, and are valid for not more than six weeks after the Parliament meets.

##### Financial Powers

The annual budget is presented in the name of the  $ \underline{\text{President}} $.

All money bills are introduced in the Parliament with the President's consent.

The Contingency Fund is at the disposal of the President. She/He advances money in case of unforeseen expenditure.

##### Judicial Powers

The President has the  $ \underline{\text{power}} $ to grant pardon, or reduce the sentence of the guilty. She/He can also pardon a death sentence.

She/He is not answerable to any court of law, other than being impeached by the Parliament.

##### Emergency Powers

An emergency is a sudden or unforeseen situation demanding immediate action. The President cannot declare an emergency without the approval of the Parliament. She/He proclaims emergency on the following grounds:

If security of the country is threatened by external aggression or armed rebellion, the situation is called a national emergency.

If the  $ \uwave{\text{administrative}} $ machinery of a state breaks down, President's  $ \uwave{\text{Rule}} $ is imposed in the state.

If the financial stability of the country is  $ \underline{\text{threatened}} $, financial emergency is declared.

#### Discretionary Powers

When no party wins an absolute majority in the Lok Sabha, the President can appoint the Prime Minister of her/his choice—a person, who she/he thinks, can command a majority in the House.

##### Vice President

The Vice President is elected indirectly by an electoral college consisting only of members from both Houses of Parliament. The term of office of Vice President is 5 years.

She/He is removed by a resolution of the Rajya Sabha, passed by a majority of its members. It has to be agreed by the Lok Sabha.

The Vice President acts on behalf of the President under the following circumstances:

If the President resigns

If the President dies in  $ \underline{\text{office}} $

If the President is  $ \underline{\text{indisposed owing to}} $ illness or  $ \underline{\text{absence}} $, or any other reason

### Powers and Functions of the Vice President

The Vice President, is the ex-officio Chairperson of the Rajya Sabha. She/He regulates debates and proceedings of the House. She/He decides the admissibility of resolutions and questions in the House in case of grave disorder. She/He heads various committees and coordinates their working.

#### Prime Minister

While the President is the  $ \underline{\text{nominal or

constitutional head}} $ of the State, the Prime Minister is the head of the  $ \underline{\text{government}} $. The Prime Minister is the pivot on which the whole constitutional machinery runs.

Dr Manmoh

Singh

### Appointment of Prime Minister and Council of Ministers

The Prime Minister is appointed by the President. In actual practice, the President is bound to appoint the leader of the majority party that wins the Lok Sabha elections as the Prime Minister. Other ministers are appointed by the President on the advice of the Prime Minister.

If no party gets an absolute majority, then two or more parties may join together and form the government. This is known as a coalition government.

##### Term of Office

The term of office for the Prime Minister and the Council of Ministers is usually five years. However, it can even be dissolved earlier if a no-confidence motion is passed against the ministry.

##### Categories of Ministers

There are three categories of ministers—Cabinet Ministers, Ministers of State and Deputy Ministers. The Cabinet Ministers form the inner core of the council. They hold important portfolios, such as finance, railways, defence, home and foreign affairs. The Ministers of State and the Deputy Ministers do not attend Cabinet meetings.

### Functions of the Prime Minister and the Cabinet

The functions and responsibilities of the Prime Minister and her/his Cabinet are as follows:

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//7daec36b-57cc-4348-87ec-3574e9313d60/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_222_1284_581_1395.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A47Z%2F-1%2F%2Fda8fb252a3b815a870ad7ebda6264185695b870c111190355dd4336ad6cdc1c5" alt="Image" width="30%" /></div>

### Debate and Discussion

What according to you is more suitable for India—Presidential system or Parliamentary system? Give reasons for your answer.

The Prime Minister with her/his Cabinet formulates policies of the government.

The entire administration of the country is carried out and coordinated by the Prime Minister and her/his Cabinet.

The President makes all major appointments on the advice of the Prime Minister and the Cabinet.

The Prime Minister coordinates the working of various departments, and is the vital link between the President and the Cabinet.

The Prime Minister distributes different portfolios and assigns duties to various ministers. In case of a conflict between a minister and the Prime Minister, the minister steps down.

The Prime Minister is the principal spokesperson and defender of the government in Parliament.

The Prime Minister represents India at international conferences, such as  $ \underline{\text{NAM}} $ (Non-Aligned Movement).

#### THE JUDICIARY

After the legislature and executive, the judiciary is the third branch or pillar of the Indian democratic setup. The Constitution of India has provided us with a single unified judiciary.

##### The Supreme Court

The Supreme Court is the guardian of the Constitution. It can interpret the Constitution and declare any law null and void, if it is not in accordance with the Constitution. The Supreme Court interprets all the laws of the union as well as the states. The Subordinate Courts, the

District Courts and the High Courts of the states all come below the Supreme Court. The Supreme Court of India is located in New Delhi.

##### Composition

Headed by the Chief Justice, the Supreme Court of India comprises a maximum of 30 other judges.

##### Did You Know?

H.J. Kania was the first Chief Justice of the Supreme Court of India. He served on this post from 1950 to 1951.

##### Appointment and Removal

The President of India appoints the Chief Justice and other judges of the Supreme Court. While appointing the judges of the Supreme Court, judges of the Supreme Court and the High Courts in the states are to be consulted. While appointing the Chief Justice, the President holds consultation with the judges of the Supreme Court and High Courts in the states.

A judge of the Supreme Court may resign from the office by writing to the President. A judge may also be removed from office through impeachment by the Parliament, on the grounds of proven misbehaviour or incapacity. The procedure to remove a judge from office is called impeachment.

##### Term of Office

Once appointed, a judge of the Supreme Court holds office till she/he attains the age of 65 years.

#### Some of the Qualifications

Must be a citizen of India

Must have been a judge of a High Court for at least 5 years or must have been an advocate of a High Court for at least 10 years

Must be, in the opinion of the President,

a distinguished jurist

Jurisdiction and Powers of the Supreme Court

##### Original Jurisdiction

Original jurisdiction extends to those cases, which the Supreme Court has the authority to hear and decide in the first instance. These are as follows:

Cases between the Government of India and the states

■ Cases between the Government of India and any state vs other states

Cases between two or more states

■ Cases involving the violation of Fundamental Rights. In such cases, the Supreme Court issues writs to enforce the Fundamental Rights.

##### Appellate Jurisdiction

Appellate cases are those which are appeals against the judgements of High Courts. Appellate cases can be the following:

Constitutional cases

Civil cases

☑ Criminal cases

##### Advisory Jurisdiction

The Supreme Court can give advice to the President on constitutional issues, when asked by the President. The President, however, is not bound to follow its advice.

##### Other Powers

Court of Record: The Supreme Court is a Court of Record. The judgements

are recorded, and are in the  $ \underline{\text{nature of precedents}} $. This means that the  $ \underline{\text{High Court}} $ and other courts are bound to give a similar decision in a similar case.

Revisory: The Supreme Court has the power to review any judgement. This provision shows that human judgement is fallible, and the court may rectify something that was misjudged.

Judicial Review: This can be defined as the power of the Supreme Court to examine the laws passed by the legislature, and the orders issued by the executive. The aim is to ensure whether they are permitted by the Constitution.

##### High Court

The High Court is at the apex of the judiciary in the State. Each High Court has jurisdiction over one or more states and union territories. All union territories fall within the jurisdiction of the High Court of a neighbouring state. Delhi has its own High Court.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//80ab4768-614f-4702-a33d-e9fb9193a1c2/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_107_961_618_1268.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F7556478df92f2256ed90290ab7e5d9ffd445454a76e86f63ce8bde3ce19d6a65" alt="Image" width="42%" /></div>

Bombay High Court

##### Composition

Each High Court has a Chief Justice, and other judges as the President may appoint. The number of judges is not fixed. It varies from state to state.

##### Appointment and Removal

The Chief Justice of the High Court is appointed by the President of India. He does this in consultation with the Chief Justice of the Supreme Court and the governor of the state concerned. The appointments of other judges are made in the same manner. However, the Chief Justice of the High Court shall also be consulted for the same.

The Chief Justice and other judges can be removed by the President's order after impeachment. The Parliament commences impeachment if it finds them guilty of proven misbehaviour or incapacity.

#### Some Qualifications

Must be a citizen of India

Should have held a judicial office in India for at least 10 years or should have been an advocate of the High Court for at least 10 years

##### Term of Office

Once appointed, a judge of the High Court serves till the age of 62. If a judge wishes, she/he can resign earlier or can be removed by the President. The same process as per which the judges of the Supreme Court are removed is followed.

#### Powers of the High Court

#### Original Jurisdiction

Original jurisdiction refers to those cases which the High Court hears and decides for the first time. These include:

Disputes concerning the Fundamental Rights

Cases involving election petitions

Cases regarding wills, marriages, divorces and contempt of court.

#### Appellate Jurisdiction

The High Court  $ \underline{\text{hears}} $ appeals, against judgements passed by the subordinate courts.

##### Subordinate Courts

Under each High Court, there are several lower courts known as subordinate courts. These courts are under the jurisdiction of the High Court.

##### District Court

The District Court and the court of the Sessions Judge are the highest courts in the district. In some places, the District Judge also acts as the Sessions Judge.

##### NYAYA PANCHAYAT

According to a press release by the Government of India on 26 August 2011:

The Government proposes to establish Nyaya Panchayats in every Gram Panchayat or a cluster of Gram Panchayats, for providing a system of fair and speedy justice, both civil and criminal, to the citizens at their doorsteps, outside the formal judicial system. The Nyaya Panchayats are proposed to be constituted through the election of the Nyaya Panchas by people residing in the area to which the jurisdiction of the Nyaya Panchayats extends. Provisions are proposed for the reservation for women, Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes to ensure their representation in the Nyaya Panchayats. The Draft Bill defines the civil, criminal and additional jurisdiction of Nyaya Panchayats. In the Draft Bill, conciliation is proposed as a primary means of dispute resolution. Further, Nyaya Sahayaks, who will assist the Nyaya Panchayat in performing their function of dispute resolution, have been proposed. Nyaya Panchayats are proposed as separate and independent dispute resolution bodies, distinct from the Gram Panchayats.

The draft Nyaya Panchayat Bill was circulated to Ministry of Law & Justice, several other Ministries/ Departments and all States/Union Territories. Based on comments received, some modifications were made in the Draft Bill.

##### Writs

The Supreme Court and the High Courts have the power to issue writs for the enforcement of the Fundamental Rights. Writs are written commands issued by a court or other legal authority to act or abstain from doing illegal acts. The examples of writs are heabeas corpus, mandamus, prohibition, quo warranto and certiorari.

#### KEY WORDS

Coalition government: a cabinet in a parliamentary system of government in which several political parties cooperate

Electoral college: formed to conduct the election of the President and the Vice President of India

Ex-officio: by virtue of the office held by a person

Fallible: capable of committing mistakes

Ordinance: temporary laws passed by the President when the Parliament is not in session, which are valid for a period of six months

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//80ab4768-614f-4702-a33d-e9fb9193a1c2/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_590_1319_741_1376.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F7d507695d2b5e1583a572919039bd4b53722cf6db8c605848e511115583d5ce6" alt="Image" width="12%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//80ab4768-614f-4702-a33d-e9fb9193a1c2/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_763_1320_911_1376.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F668414615cbb4c3703596f02647f85e05db1d92f73f1a01a028e4936fab0664d" alt="Image" width="12%" /></div>

Parliamentary Democracy: a country or a state where people elect a government

Precedent: a legal case, which establishes a rule that another court may utilise in deciding similar cases

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//80ab4768-614f-4702-a33d-e9fb9193a1c2/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_1139_1503_1169_1550.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2Fb32c063da7dd5300482c5d4924734e5e65c1177b6da89240b510c9159282cd1f" alt="Image" width="2%" /></div>

Proclamation of Emergency: An emergency is proclaimed by the President if she/he is convinced that the security of the country is threatened in case of an armed rebellion war or external aggression. Fundamental Rights of the citizens are suspended during the period of emergency. Proportional Representation: a voting system aimed at securing a match between the percentage of votes received by a candidate in the elections, and the seats secured in the legislature. Secret Ballot System: a system in which the choice of the voter is kept confidential. Single transferable vote: a voting system based on proportional representation and preferential

### I Have Democratic Values!

#### Theme: Democratic Government

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//80ab4768-614f-4702-a33d-e9fb9193a1c2/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_1059_473_1142_585.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A36Z%2F-1%2F%2F2bb039a7d854ca655a6a48687bc99213cce4bf3aafe39c11f17b945f24d020e5" alt="Image" width="6%" /></div>

Democracy is a form of government in which people choose leaders and representatives by voting and everyone is treated equally and has equal rights. India is a representative democracy. It means that in our country, eligible people vote for others to carry out the business of government. We elect them to be our voice.

##### Activity 1

You have been assigned the role of a representative for your constituency. You are getting ready for the election campaign, which will start soon. Write and give a speech about what you would offer if ‘elected’.

#### Activity 2

Role-play: After you are elected as an MP for your constituency, you have been asked to design a new park to celebrate the 100th year celebration of Independence Day in India. You can decide how big the park should be and what will be included in it. You have an unlimited budget. Perform a role-play using dialogues and actions based on the key principles of working in a representative democracy:

• Your whole group discusses the park design and facilities that it should offer.

• The group then votes and selects two most suitable people to work on the design.

• The two elected representatives can consult the others for advice at any time.

• The final project can be inaugurated by the Prime Minister and declared open for the people.

##### Activity 3

The queen is the mother of the entire population of an ant colony. Find out how ‘government’ works in insect groups such as ants. Can you describe how these groups work using government analogies?

##### Activity 4

Voting and elections are essential activities in a democracy. Elections are all about numbers and how many votes a party gets usually decides whether it will form the government or not.

## 15 The United Nations

#### Political Life Alive!

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//bb750166-0d09-401f-9919-fc06b8cb9a20/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_117_290_829_590.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F585e62a0cf38a41fe678e228978de1764c39b2701c7eaad38791248deb2d82c9" alt="Image" width="59%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//bb750166-0d09-401f-9919-fc06b8cb9a20/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_990_227_1118_316.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2F7ae0cb9c4b2972e96bdef4ff65ecb65065410655b3096f9bad3d2d38eef24ef4" alt="Image" width="10%" /></div>

The General Assembly comprises all 193 members of the United Nations (UN). It is the closest thing to a 'world parliament'.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//bb750166-0d09-401f-9919-fc06b8cb9a20/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_435_194_699_437.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F09af82e4f93b4c8c1a2933d9eaded5ffe395dc0421fb9ee82b1909d3ed638316" alt="Image" width="22%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//bb750166-0d09-401f-9919-fc06b8cb9a20/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_784_223_1038_445.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F5d322b54ca8bf384a8b8f1146afe414f0869f56d80e19bd0e36bed329c0bbf3d" alt="Image" width="21%" /></div>

☐ Constructing roads

The beginning of the 20th century witnessed World War I, the horror and tragedy of which devastated the world. Millions lost their lives while an equal number of people were maimed or injured. The destruction was unimaginable. There was an overwhelming desire for an end to the war and establishment of peace. The League of Nations was founded for this very purpose. Its opening session was held in 1919.

The League of Nations was the first international organisation responsible for ensuring peace and cooperation between nations of the world. In its early years, the League was able to maintain peace and prevent conflicts. However, in the 1930s its success waned as the Axis Powers (Germany, Italy and Japan) gained influence, which eventually led to the start of World War II in 1939.

Preparations for such an organisation had begun long back in 1941, while the war was in full swing. To avoid such a war in the future, the United Nations (UN) was formed. The American President, Franklin Roosevelt first coined the term 'United Nations'.

##### THE ATLANTIC CHARTER

On 14 August 1941, the British Prime Minister, Winston Churchill and President Roosevelt met on board a battleship and signed the Atlantic Charter. Some of the proposals drafted in this Charter by Winston Churchill and Franklin Roosevelt became the basis for the establishment of the United Nations. In January 1942, 26 countries pledged their support to the Atlantic Charter by signing the Declaration by United Nations. On 25 April 1945, the United Nations Conference on International

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//bb750166-0d09-401f-9919-fc06b8cb9a20/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_599_1048_1097_1404.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2Fdfd602c1332182daba78456d1a418bb44b588ec804488607f0f1e77f678b65c2" alt="Image" width="41%" /></div>

▶ Franklin Roosevelt and Winston Churchill aboard the ship for the signing of the Atlantic Charter

Organization began in San Francisco, and was attended by delegates of 50 nations involved in drafting the Charter of the UN. The UN officially came into existence on 24 October 1945, which is celebrated as United Nations Day all over the world.

The United Nations began functioning with 51 nations as original members. However, the UN Charter has made provisions for the admission of new members. The headquarters of the UN are in New York, USA. The UN has adopted English, French, Chinese, Russian, Arabic and Spanish as its official languages. Funds for the successful functioning of the UN are contributed by the member nations.

### OBJECTIVES OF THE UNITED NATIONS

The preamble of the UN charter outlines the objectives of the UN. These are as follows:

Maintenance of international peace and security

Promotion of human rights for people all over the world

Protection of future generations from the devastation of wars

Establishment of equal rights for all persons

Promotion of justice, freedom and social progress for all its member states

Respect for international laws and international treaties

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//bb750166-0d09-401f-9919-fc06b8cb9a20/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_222_1331_322_1470.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2Ff90cf799a0552e81fdcae7258575d0bbf98b6ef53a4a8dc7e3ddc9be8643c25b" alt="Image" width="8%" /></div>

### Debate and Discussion CENTURY SKILLS

communication

critical thinking: reasoning

How has the formation of the UN prevented the occurrence of a Third World War?

### STRUCTURE OF THE UNITED NATIONS

The UN has six principal organs—the General Assembly, the Security Council, the International Court of Justice, the Economic and Social Council, the Secretariat and the Trusteeship Council.

##### The General Assembly

This is the main deliberative assembly of the UN. All UN member states are members of the General Assembly. The Assembly meets once every year. It is a kind of a parliament of nations. Each member state has only one vote. Decisions are made by a majority vote. But important resolutions, such as those concerning peace and security issues, require a two-thirds majority.

##### The Security Council

This is often considered the most important organ of the UN. It has been given the responsibility of maintaining peace and security among countries. While other organs of the UN can only make ‘recommendations’ to member states, the Security Council has the power to make binding decisions that member states are required to carry out according to the terms of the Charter.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//bb750166-0d09-401f-9919-fc06b8cb9a20/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_639_1161_1132_1495.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F57afe03a94a319575417c2a23e14e572fc67e26cf47fbf6d791d8d15e45f9cd6" alt="Image" width="41%" /></div>

The Security Council

There are 15 member countries that make up the Security Council. Among these 15 countries, five are permanent members—the USA, the UK, France, Russia and China. There are also 10 non-permanent members who are elected to the Security Council by the General Assembly and their term lasts for 2 years.

The five permanent members exercise a special power called the veto power. Veto is a negative vote by any one of the permanent members. When a permanent member vetoes a resolution, it is cancelled. This means that the consent of all five permanent members is necessary for all decisions made by the Security Council of the UN.

##### The International Court of Justice

This is the primary judicial organ of the United Nations. The Court comprises 15 judges who are elected for a 9-year term. The judges are from different countries. No two judges can be from the same country. The International Court of Justice has its headquarters at The Hague (Netherlands).

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//bb750166-0d09-401f-9919-fc06b8cb9a20/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_50_1013_546_1467.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F854992940b9488bf71e5fce0ac2fac32084b80a710945a3e17d6f958274bbf4e" alt="Image" width="41%" /></div>

The International Court of Justice

### The Economic and Social Council (ECOSOC)

This organ of the UN assists the General Assembly in promoting international and social cooperation and development. It has 54 members, elected by the General Assembly for a 3-year term.

##### The Secretariat

The Secretariat is headed by the Secretary-General who is elected for a term of 5 years by the General Assembly. It is the duty of the Secretariat to organise conferences, draft reports and prepare estimates for budget allocation. It provides studies, information and facilities needed by the UN member states for their meetings. It also carries out tasks as directed by the UN General Assembly, Security Council and other UN bodies.

##### The Trusteeship Council

This organ of the UN was created to supervise the administration of Trust Territories, which were not completely independent. Hence, these territories were placed under the administration of seven member states. By 1994, all Trust Territories attained independence or self-government.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//bb750166-0d09-401f-9919-fc06b8cb9a20/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_581_1123_1105_1458.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2F87d677ef2f527a1d205f8b24b599adcc87ec5ed554abfd5be01785b0e303ecec" alt="Image" width="44%" /></div>

The Trusteeship Council

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//edb21baf-964e-44cf-8ef6-ee97bd5e0c80/markdown_0/imgs/img_in_image_box_49_5_1132_1192.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe92ab6d8c0c726a99cc1d2a5bdc0a50e9af97deb85ddee0f1d426303251fa318" alt="Image" width="91%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><div style="text-align: center;">▶ A flow chart showing the functions of the organs of the United Nations</div> </div>

##### UNITED NATIONS TODAY

The main function of the UN today is to maintain peace and security for all its member states. The flow chart (given above) mentions the functions of the various organs of the UN. Some of the UN's other functions are:

The UN has peacekeeping forces, which are made up of personnel from its member states. These peacekeepers are often sent to regions where an armed conflict has recently ended to discourage combatants from resuming war.

The UN aims to protect human rights.

It provides technical assistance and helps to improve judicial structures and draft constitutions.

It provides food, drinking water, shelter as well as humanitarian services to people displaced by war, famine and natural disasters.

The UN plays an integral part in social and economic progress through its United Nations Development Programme.

### Achievements of the United Nations

The UN has not always been successful in its attempt to prevent wars. However, it has taken effective action to restore peace.

The UN strives to protect and preserve human rights all over the world.

It imposed sanctions against South Africa, which helped in changing the policies of the South African government to end apartheid.

The UN has been successful in the areas of health, child welfare, labour and education through its various agencies.

There have been active efforts to end the nuclear arms race and promote the use of nuclear energy for peaceful purposes.

The world needs organisations like the UN more than ever today, especially when the threat of terrorism and communal hatred and discord looms over us.

### AGENCIES OF THE UNITED NATIONS

You have read earlier that maintaining international peace and security in the world is not the only function of the United Nations. Some of its other objectives are to help nations work together to improve the lives of poor people, to conquer hunger, disease and illiteracy and to encourage respect for each other's rights and freedoms. It also focuses on developing friendly relations between nations and coordinating among nations to achieve these goals. Several agencies have been set up to achieve these goals. Apart from the six principal organs discussed earlier, the UN has several agencies and bodies to carry out various functions on its behalf. The functions of some of the key UN agencies are discussed hereunder.

## The United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization (UNESCO)

The UNESCO came into existence in November 1946.

It has its headquarters in Paris, France.

The UNESCO’s mission is to contribute to peace and security in the world by promoting collaboration among nations through education, science and culture. This objective is based on the belief that the best way of preventing war is through educating people on the benefits of peace.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//edb21baf-964e-44cf-8ef6-ee97bd5e0c80/markdown_1/imgs/img_in_image_box_556_1131_1068_1467.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A33Z%2F-1%2F%2Fba28e116ccca633c3db468b1cb02694fbd77e856b6ae0792ffcaf0aae5c5e704" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>

UNESCO office for Water Education in the Netherlands

### United Nations Children's Fund (UNICEF)

Originally called the United Nations International Children's Emergency Fund, the UNICEF was established in 1946.

Its main function was to provide food, clothing and healthcare to children who were faced with famine and disease in the aftermath of World War II.

The words ‘international’ and ‘emergency’ were later dropped and it came to be known as the United Nations Children's Fund.

Since its establishment, the UNICEF has taken up numerous initiatives and programmes to carry out its mission.

In 1949, the first UNICEF greeting card was created.

■ It launched a worldwide fundraising activity for the UNICEF which continues to this day.

Famous personalities are also appointed as ambassadors to focus global attention on the UNICEF's work.

#### Connecting Past with Present

### World Health Organization (WHO)

WHO was established on 7 April 1948. This day is observed every year as the World Health Day.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//edb21baf-964e-44cf-8ef6-ee97bd5e0c80/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_640_346_1153_744.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A34Z%2F-1%2F%2F19036178817fcd91c4a5b6ab647d2e0f8ed1cbe388c3be36c81a1bcaf5511472" alt="Image" width="43%" /></div>

The Indian government has adopted measures such as regular inspection of work premises to eliminate child labour.

The goal of this agency is health for all.

It values health as both a fundamental human right and a sound social investment.

The WHO has its headquarters in Geneva, Switzerland.

### International Labour Organization (ILO)

The ILO was founded in 1919 to promote rights at work and encourage decent employment opportunities.

It became the first specialised agency of the UN.

##### Did You Know?

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//edb21baf-964e-44cf-8ef6-ee97bd5e0c80/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_850_483_941_583.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A35Z%2F-1%2F%2Fbc54c394095d48f65968c4c4db63f2b00bc5f27152c69f5076f8062f5d14bad6" alt="Image" width="7%" /></div>

The United Nations Development Programme (UNDP) was formed in 1965. It advocates change and connects the countries to knowledge, experience and resources to help people build a better life. It has its headquarters at New York, USA.

It has its headquarters in Geneva, Switzerland.

##### FUNCTIONS OF THE AGENCIES

The agencies discussed so far perform different functions. Study the table given below to know about these functions.

### SOME OTHER IMPORTANT AGENCIES OF THE UN

The World Bank: This provides loans and technical assistance to developing countries to reduce poverty and advance sustainable economic growth.

The International Monetary Fund (IMF): It facilitates international monetary cooperation and financial stability.

The International Civil Aviation Organization (ICAO): This agency sets international standards necessary for the safety, security and efficiency of air transport.

The International Telecommunication Union (ITU): This agency fosters international cooperation for the improvement and use of all kinds of telecommunication.

The World Meteorological Organization (WMO): This promotes scientific research on atmosphere and climate change.

The World Trade Organization (WTO): It oversees international trade and cooperates in providing assistance in exports through the International Trade Centre.

#### KEYWORDS

Apartheid: a system of racial discrimination in South Africa, wherein only White people had political and social rights and privileges; coloured people had no rights and lived segregated from the Whites in poor conditions

Child care centres: centres which provide medical assistance to young mothers and their newborn children

Embargo: economic and diplomatic sanctions against a hostile or aggressive country meaning a ban on economic trade or cordial relationships with that country

League of Nations: the first international peacekeeping organisation formed to prevent wars after the devastation and destruction during World War I

Resolution: a formal statement, proposal or agreement by a group or council

Sweatshops: a factory or workshop, especially in the clothing industry, where manual workers are employed at very low wages for long hours and poor conditions

Veto: power to vote against a resolution by any one of the five permanent members of the Security Council which cancels the resolution

World Health Day: celebrated on 7 April to create awareness about good health and improve standards of health all over the world

# Project-based Learning Countering the Problem of Misinformation and Disinformation

DRIVING QUESTION: How should we avoid the potential harmful

consequences of misinformation and disinformation?

Duration:

4 Weeks

##### Learning Outcomes

After the completion of the project, learners will be able to:

analyse the problems that arise with the spread of misinformation and disinformation.

evaluate the ways in which getting influenced by misinformation/disinformation can be avoided, both socially and academically.

distinguish news items from advertisements online.

assess if an information is credible or dubious.

practice their new found skill of sorting information by going through tweets on Twitter, comments section in online newspapers and diverse views in opinion columns.

#### 21st Century Skills

▶ critical thinking—analysing, reasoning, problem-solving, decision-making

collaboration—brainstorming,

participatory decision-making

communication—reading, speaking, listening, writing

life skills—planning and execution

problem-solving

▶ general awareness

social and cross-cultural interaction

technological literacy

##### Curriculum Connections

▶ general knowledge ▶ political science

life skills

computers

▶ english

## A Note to the Teacher

art-integrated learning

The purpose of this project is to make learners develop the necessary skills to effectively manage the problem of misinformation and disinformation. The learners will be able to judge the credibility of information that floods our computers, tablets and smartphones.

Beginning with studying the impact that the spread of misinformation and disinformation has, the students will move on to identifying actual news items via a vis advertisements. They will be made aware of supposed 'news items' circulating on the Internet and discern if the information is credible or dubious. They be exposed to varied tweets, comments and opinions of the people on popular news topics, and asked to give reasons why they prefer one over the other.

To start with, you may divide the class into groups based on individual projects. You can allot time for completing the activities. One representative from each group will present the observations and answers to questions.

##### Related Vocabulary

credible: believable based on evidence, convincing

discern: to recognise or identify, to perceive something using your senses

disinformation: false information that is spread deliberately

impressionable: easily influenced or persuaded

misinformation: a wrong piece of information

prolific: producing a large amount of something

teem: to be filled to overflowing, to be full of something

viral: (in this case) used to signify a piece of information that spreads rapidly over the Internet

##### Let's Get Started: What can happen if false information/news spreads?

The learners are to empathise with the possible consequences of spread of misinformation/disinformation at a local level.

##### As a group, imagine a scenario

As a group, brainstorm and come up with an imaginary piece of 'fake news' in your school.

Discuss what will happen if this news spreads.

• Come up with the consequences, and consequences of consequences.

Make a note of each consequence.

##### An example of the spread of misinformation disinformation:

Fake information: 'The gardener was seen trespassing in the Principal's room, and potentially stole something.

Consequence 1: People in the school start avoiding the gardener. They whisper amongst themselves and spread the fake information further.

Consequence 2: Someone tells the gardener what is being said, and he is humiliated.

Consequence 3: The gardener confronts the Principal/The gardener is called to the Principal's office.

Consequence 4: The Principal has misplaced a recent school trophy and chooses to blame the gardener. The gardener loses his/her job.

Consequence 5: The Principal gives the gardener benefit of doubt, but now will remain suspicious of him/her.

##### Write and enact a play

Based on your brainstorming session in the class, write a play that includes many examples of misinformation/disinformation you have encountered or can think of. You can even write this play as a comedy of errors without losing the seriousness that is conveyed. Enact this play in your school.

##### Distinguish News Items from Advertisements Online

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//27793129-984d-413b-bb22-f8ff20471ce2/markdown_3/imgs/img_in_image_box_969_1032_1129_1087.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A37Z%2F-1%2F%2Fe1e7f12544a2fb11dd8d92135cc54a1d23ac09cbc3bfa0f5e88292037cee49bb" alt="Image" width="13%" /></div>

Many news websites try to sell a product in the guise of a news item. It becomes difficult to understand the ulterior motive behind a piece of information.

##### As partners in the project

The learners are encouraged to explore news websites on the Internet. Most of these websites have news items and advertisements. The learners are expected to distinguish between a news article and an advertisement. The teacher may help the learners to access these sections on a news website:

a traditional advertisement a news story an advertisement disguised as a news story

The learners are expected to determine the nature of each one of the above. They have to clearly outline the characteristics of each. Some of these characteristics are listed as follows.

##### An advertisement:

It has 'Ad Choices' and 'Stop Seeing This Ad' buttons on the top right corner. It has a company logo, a coupon code or 'limited time offer' written on it.

## A news story:

There is no small 'x' cancel button on any corner of a news story.

An advertisement disguised as a news story:

An advertisement that is presented as a news story, often has 'Sponsored Content' written on it.

##### Visualise what you have learnt

On a big piece of paper, draw and write an advertisement, a news story and an advertisement is a story. Add all the features that you noticed in your web search on each.

##### Sources of Information

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//27793129-984d-413b-bb22-f8ff20471ce2/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_939_325_1097_396.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A38Z%2F-1%2F%2F6e45330c6324c5fd61077b8c7b677275ebdb54eb5445ed72ac5478442d4d7a5a" alt="Image" width="13%" /></div>

How can learners distinguish between legitimate and dubious information? By asking one simple question: Where did this information I am looking at/hearing come from?

##### As a group:

The teacher provides a dubious picture/video that is circulating on social media these days. The learners are expected to question the viability of the information given. Some sound arguments that they can give are as follows:

• They know nothing about the credentials of the person who posted this picture/video.

• They may claim that the picture/video provides no proof of the information it is giving.

##### As individuals:

The teacher may show other examples of dubious information, along with credible stories to the learners. Each learner will maintain a sheet of paper and write the reasons why she/he considers a particular piece of information dubious or credible. A class discussion may take place after each piece of information is shown.

##### Practice Makes a Person Perfect

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//27793129-984d-413b-bb22-f8ff20471ce2/markdown_4/imgs/img_in_image_box_924_858_1095_931.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A38Z%2F-1%2F%2Fa50172d41bba1f324a5ec05fb3ff02eed0d32f3c26284eea6ea1e5ca03663424" alt="Image" width="14%" /></div>

This week the students can do a range of activities, so that their skills of sorting information can be honed further. These are as follows:

• Surf on Twitter: With the help of the teacher/parents, the learners may go through tweets on Twitter. They may select at least five tweets that they consider trustworthy. These may be added to the practice file, along with the reasons why they consider them credible.

Browse through Comments: The learners may access a news article online and go through the comments of the readers. They may explain if they will use these comments in their research report.

- Opposing Views in the Opinion Column: The learners may evaluate two different views on the same topic in the Opinion Column of a newspaper. They may decide which one they agree with and give reasons for their choice.

##### School Newspaper

As a class, the learners will compile a newspaper that covers the news from across their school in the past month. The class may be divided into groups, and each group allotted one area that they can report on, such as academics, sports, dance and music, art and painting and so on. Each group will come up with credible stories, checking all facts that go in the write up. They are to maintain an evidence document that supports what they have written. The evidence may include interviews, inspection reports, photographs and other documents.

#### Worksheet 4

1. Study the given picture and answer the following questions.

5. What took place during the movement?

II. Differentiate between the following by completing the table.

III. Give reasons for the following statements.

1. Gandhiji suspended the Civil-disobedience movement in 1931.

2. Sir Stafford Cripps was sent to India.

3. The Quit India Movement was considered to be an important landmark in India's struggle for freedom.

# MODEL TEST PAPER 2

Time Allowed: 1 Hour and 30 Minutes

Total Marks = 40

 $ (10 \times 1 = 10) $

#### 1. Choose the correct option.

1. Two statements are given in the question below as Assertion (A) and Reasoning (R). Read the statements and choose the correct option.

Assertion (A): The Revolt of 1857 failed.

Reasoning (R): Main reason being the lack of coordination, unity and centralised leadership

a. Both (A) and (R) are true and (R) is the correct explanation for (A).

b. Both (A) and (R) are true but (R)  $ \underline{\text{is not}} $ the correct explanation for (A).

c. Only (A) is true and (R) is false.  $ \Box $ d. Both (A) and (R) are false.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//829e3601-9ed6-4c7f-aba2-227f6cdca2b1/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_1065_284_1120_385.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A59Z%2F-1%2F%2F6c6253e1057ffc34cfb4b13a1ec337b0d05916bb03351e084bcce21b9c61f876" alt="Image" width="4%" /></div>

2. Two statements are given in the question below as Assertion (A) and Reasoning (R). Read the statements and choose the correct option.

Assertion (A): Many Indian reformers emerged during the 19th century.

Reasoning (R): They realised that if they have to defeat the British, they needed to reform the Indian society.

a. Both (A) and (R) are true and (R) is the correct explanation for (A).

b. Both (A) and (R) are true but (R) is not the correct explanation for (A).

c. Only (A) is true and (R) is false.  $ \Box $ d. Both (A) and (R) are false.

3. Which of the following was not a literary figure?

a. Tarabai Shinde

c. Raja Ravi Verma

b. Subramania Bharati

d. Sarohini Naidu

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//829e3601-9ed6-4c7f-aba2-227f6cdca2b1/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_1065_660_1119_737.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A59Z%2F-1%2F%2Ffc4ce72403dcfd0f4fae4af049ad0e1786edf1981e07c27c7968cef515459a67" alt="Image" width="4%" /></div>

4. An Old Man's Hope was written by

a. Lord Dalhousie

c. Lord Rippon

5. Two statements are given in the question below as Assertion (A) and Reasoning (R). Read the statements and choose the correct option.

Assertion (A): Moderates in the INC were considered to be microscopic minority. Reasoning (R): The leaders of the moderates represented only a small section of the population and the masses at large remained unaffected by their activities.

a. Both (A) and (R) are true and (R) is the correct explanation for (A).

b. Both (A) and (R) are true but (R) is not the correct explanation for (A).

c. Only (A) is true and (R) is false.  $ \Box $ d. Both (A) and (R) are false.

### II. State whether the following statements are true or false. Correct the false statements.  $ (4 \times 2 = 8) $

1. IMF provides loans and technical assistance to developing countries.

2. The UN has not always been successful in its attempt to prevent wars.

3. The UNESCO came into existence in September 1946.

4. The UN has peacekeeping forces, which are made up of personnel from its member states.

III. With reference to the Partition of Bengal, answer the following questions.

$(4\times2=8)$

1. What is the officially declared reason and the actual reason for the partition of Bengal?

2. When was Bengal partitioned?

3. Name the two movements launched by the INC in reply to the Bengal partition.

4. How did the British Government retaliate the activities of the revolutionaries?

IV. Study the given picture and answer the following questions.

1. Identify the person in the picture.

(5x1=5)

2. Where was her kingdom located?

3. Why did she join the Revolt of 1857?

4. Who supported her during her offensive strike against the Company?

5. What happened to her during the revolt?

V. Draw a flow chart showing the different organs of the UN and one main function of each.  $ (5 \times 1 = 5) $

# IMPORTANT STEPS TO CHOOSING A MASK

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a85c4261-f917-4543-8b26-da9e04919806/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_93_169_660_450.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A39Z%2F-1%2F%2F5c842c662488dd573040d7c2d8ca8a42b6e5ef47356fd79b8da657b57d713d44" alt="Image" width="47%" /></div>

##### Make sure your mask fits

• Pick a mask with multiple layers to keep your respiratory droplets in and others' out.

• Choose a mask with a nose wire to prevent air from leaking out of the top.

##### For extra protection

Wear a disposable mask under a cloth mask

Knot and tuck ear loops of a 3-ply mask

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a85c4261-f917-4543-8b26-da9e04919806/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_96_658_373_966.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A40Z%2F-1%2F%2Fd59394a7491b963834b611190f6dc1f5b5c15f39d9f832ed5e71185aefda6f14" alt="Image" width="23%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a85c4261-f917-4543-8b26-da9e04919806/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_452_637_734_977.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A40Z%2F-1%2F%2Fefb0b102dcfd3e61f0b44da151fa6fc8d8ccf274ea04f43cd57ce0375a4c3f39" alt="Image" width="23%" /></div>

Use a mask fitter or brace over a disposable or cloth mask

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a85c4261-f917-4543-8b26-da9e04919806/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_773_661_1092_977.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A40Z%2F-1%2F%2Fdab52b03299eb9c52ea56c61e7ea0de13156002ee75f1a7868c03d373581f03d" alt="Image" width="26%" /></div>

### Respirators must form a seal to the face to work properly.

• Follow manufacturer instructions.

• Check for markings on  $ \underline{\text{N95, KN95}} $, and other respirators that indicate the product is authentic.

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a85c4261-f917-4543-8b26-da9e04919806/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_743_1003_1107_1347.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A40Z%2F-1%2F%2Fbdc16512cc648aa41318c66e78590b0cdfb44e8b2d4fd1ec149fc923172041b8" alt="Image" width="30%" /></div>

<div style="text-align: center;"><img src="https://pplines-online.bj.bcebos.com/deploy/official/paddleocr/pp-ocr-vl-16-online//a85c4261-f917-4543-8b26-da9e04919806/markdown_2/imgs/img_in_image_box_88_1368_328_1506.jpg?authorization=bce-auth-v1%2FALTAKDN8mY5KlNI7zaRpLmOqrw%2F2026-06-10T19%3A44%3A40Z%2F-1%2F%2F2c4cc38afe437203e9fc2975b038d650c51af77a220b4a0434277ddfa1e29d1e" alt="Image" width="20%" /></div>
